<th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">Country</th>

</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">Role</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Naval_warfare" title="Naval warfare">Naval warfare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Power_projection" title="Power projection">power projection</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massive_retaliation" title="Massive retaliation">nuclear deterrence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sealift" title="Sealift">sealift</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">Size</th>
<td>323,197 active duty personnel<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-status-2">[2]</a></sup><br/>
108,515 reserve personnel<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-status-2">[2]</a></sup><br/>
280 deployable ships<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-status-2">[2]</a></sup><br/>
430 <a href="/wiki/List_of_current_ships_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="List of current ships of the United States Navy">total ships</a><br/>
3,700+ aircraft<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-status-2">[2]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Navy" title="United States Department of the Navy">Dept. of the Navy</a> <small>(since 1798)</small></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>

<th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">Anchor, <i>Constitution</i>, and Eagle</th>
<td><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anchor,_Constitution,_and_Eagle.svg"><img alt="Anchor, Constitution, and Eagle.svg" data-file-height="524" data-file-width="500" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Anchor%2C_Constitution%2C_and_Eagle.svg/100px-Anchor%2C_Constitution%2C_and_Eagle.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Anchor%2C_Constitution%2C_and_Eagle.svg/150px-Anchor%2C_Constitution%2C_and_Eagle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Anchor%2C_Constitution%2C_and_Eagle.svg/200px-Anchor%2C_Constitution%2C_and_Eagle.svg.png 2x" width="100"/></a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>United States Navy</b> (<b>USN</b>) is the <a href="/wiki/Naval_warfare" title="Naval warfare">naval warfare</a> service branch of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">United States Armed Forces</a> and one of the seven <a href="/wiki/Uniformed_services_of_the_United_States" title="Uniformed services of the United States">uniformed services of the United States</a>. The U.S. Navy is the largest, most capable <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">navy</a> in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> with the highest combined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_with_warships#Warship_table" title="List of countries with warships">battle fleet tonnage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The U.S. Navy has the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a> fleet, with <a href="/wiki/List_of_aircraft_carriers_in_service" title="List of aircraft carriers in service">eleven in service</a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Kitty_Hawk_(CV-63)" title="USS Kitty Hawk (CV-63)">one</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_fleet" title="Reserve fleet">reserve fleet</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and two new carriers under construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The service has 322,421 personnel on active duty and 107,577 in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_Reserve" title="United States Navy Reserve">Navy Reserve</a>. It has 276 deployable combat vessels and more than 3,700 operational aircraft as of June 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-status-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The U.S. Navy traces its origins to the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Navy" title="Continental Navy">Continental Navy</a>, which was established during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> and was effectively disbanded as a separate entity shortly thereafter. It played a major role in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> by blockading the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederacy</a> and seizing control of its rivers. It played the central role in the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> defeat of Imperial Japan. The 21st century U.S. Navy maintains a sizable global presence, deploying in strength in such areas as the Western <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/Blue-water_navy" title="Blue-water navy">blue-water navy</a> with the ability to <a href="/wiki/Power_projection" title="Power projection">project force</a> onto the <a href="/wiki/Littoral_zone" title="Littoral zone">littoral regions</a> of the world, engage in forward deployments during peacetime and rapidly respond to regional crises, making it a frequent actor in U.S. foreign and military policy.</p>
<p>The Navy is administratively managed by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Navy" title="United States Department of the Navy">Department of the Navy</a>, which is headed by the civilian <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="United States Secretary of the Navy">Secretary of the Navy</a>. The Department of the Navy is itself a division of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">Department of Defense</a>, which is headed by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense" title="United States Secretary of Defense">Secretary of Defense</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Naval_Operations" title="Chief of Naval Operations">Chief of Naval Operations</a> (CNO) is a four-star admiral and the senior naval officer of the Department of the Navy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mission">Mission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Mission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The mission of the Navy is to maintain, train and equip combat-ready Naval forces capable of winning wars, deterring aggression and maintaining freedom of the seas.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>Mission statement of the United States Navy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MissionOfTheNavy_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-MissionOfTheNavy-14">[14]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>The U.S. Navy is a seaborne branch of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_United_States" title="Military of the United States">military of the United States</a>. The Navy's three primary areas of responsibility:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The preparation of naval forces necessary for the effective prosecution of war.</li>
<li>The maintenance of naval aviation, including land-based naval aviation, air transport essential for naval operations, and all air weapons and air techniques involved in the operations and activities of the Navy.</li>
<li>The development of <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a>, weapons, tactics, technique, organization, and equipment of naval combat and service elements.</li>
</ul>
<p>U.S. Navy training manuals state that the mission of the U.S. Armed Forces is "to prepare and conduct prompt and sustained combat operations in support of the national interest. "As part of that establishment, the U.S. Navy's functions comprise <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_control" title="Sea control">sea control</a>, <a href="/wiki/Power_projection" title="Power projection">power projection</a> and <a href="/wiki/Massive_retaliation" title="Massive retaliation">nuclear deterrence</a>, in addition to "<a href="/wiki/Sealift" title="Sealift">sealift</a>" duties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="History of the United States Navy">History of the United States Navy</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>It follows then as certain as that night succeeds the day, that without a decisive naval force we can do nothing definitive, and with it, everything honorable and glorious.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FamousNavyQuotes_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FamousNavyQuotes-17">[17]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>The Navy was rooted in the colonial seafaring tradition, which produced a large community of sailors, captains, and shipbuilders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> In the early stages of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> had its own <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Naval_Militia" title="Massachusetts Naval Militia">Massachusetts Naval Militia</a>. The rational for establishing a national navy was debated in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress" title="Second Continental Congress">Second</a> <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">Continental Congress</a>. Supporters argued that a navy would protect shipping, defend the coast, and make it easier to seek out support from foreign countries. Detractors countered that challenging the British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>, then the world's preeminent naval power, was a foolish undertaking. <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">Commander in Chief</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> resolved the debate when he commissioned the ocean-going schooner <a href="/wiki/USS_Hannah" title="USS Hannah">USS <i>Hannah</i></a> to interdict British merchant ships, and reported the captures to the Congress. On 13 October 1775, the Continental Congress authorized the purchase of two vessels to be armed for a cruise against British merchant ships; this resolution created the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Navy" title="Continental Navy">Continental Navy</a> and is considered the first establishment of the U.S. Navy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Continental_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Continental-19">[19]</a></sup> The Continental Navy achieved mixed results; it was successful in a number of engagements and raided many British merchant vessels, but it lost twenty-four of its vessels<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-love_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-love-20">[20]</a></sup> and at one point was reduced to two in active service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-howarth_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-howarth-21">[21]</a></sup> In August 1785, after the Revolutionary War had drawn to a close, <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_Confederation" title="Congress of the Confederation">Congress</a> had sold <a href="/wiki/USS_Alliance_(1778)" title="USS Alliance (1778)"><i>Alliance</i></a>, the last ship remaining in the Continental Navy due to a lack of funds to maintain the ship or support a navy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alliance_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alliance-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AbbotVIPICXV_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-AbbotVIPICXV-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1972, the Chief of Naval Operations, Admiral <a href="/wiki/Elmo_Zumwalt" title="Elmo Zumwalt">Elmo Zumwalt</a>, authorized the Navy to celebrate its birthday on 13 October to honor the establishment of the Continental Navy in 1775.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Navy_Birthday_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_Navy_Birthday-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Continental_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Continental-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_re-establishment_to_the_Civil_War">From re-establishment to the Civil War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: From re-establishment to the Civil War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USSConstellationVsInsurgente.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3946" data-file-width="4996" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/USSConstellationVsInsurgente.jpg/220px-USSConstellationVsInsurgente.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/USSConstellationVsInsurgente.jpg/330px-USSConstellationVsInsurgente.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/USSConstellationVsInsurgente.jpg/440px-USSConstellationVsInsurgente.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USSConstellationVsInsurgente.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Constellation_vs_L%27Insurgente" title="USS Constellation vs L'Insurgente">USS <i>Constellation</i> vs <i>L'Insurgente</i></a> during the <a href="/wiki/Quasi-War" title="Quasi-War">Quasi-War</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The United States was without a navy for nearly a decade, a state of affairs that exposed U.S. maritime merchant ships to a series of attacks by the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a>. The sole armed maritime presence between 1790 and the launching of the U.S. Navy's first warships in 1797 was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Revenue_Cutter_Service" title="U.S. Revenue Cutter Service">U.S. Revenue Cutter Service</a> (USRCS), the primary predecessor of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Coast_Guard" title="U.S. Coast Guard">U.S. Coast Guard</a>. Although the USRCS conducted operations against the pirates, their depredations far outstripped its abilities and Congress passed the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Act_of_1794" title="Naval Act of 1794">Naval Act of 1794</a> that established a permanent standing navy on 27 March 1794.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-US-25">[25]</a></sup> The Naval Act ordered the construction and manning of <a href="/wiki/Original_six_frigates_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Original six frigates of the United States Navy">six frigates</a> and, by October 1797,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-love_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-love-20">[20]</a></sup> the first three were brought into service: <a href="/wiki/USS_United_States_(1797)" title="USS United States (1797)">USS <i>United States</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Constellation_(1797)" title="USS Constellation (1797)">USS <i>Constellation</i></a>, and <a href="/wiki/USS_Constitution" title="USS Constitution">USS <i>Constitution</i></a>. Due to his strong posture on having a strong standing Navy during this period, <a href="/wiki/John_Adams" title="John Adams">John Adams</a> is "often called the father of the American Navy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In 1798–99 the Navy was involved in an undeclared <a href="/wiki/Quasi-War" title="Quasi-War">Quasi-War</a> with France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> From 1801 to 1805, in the <a href="/wiki/First_Barbary_War" title="First Barbary War">First Barbary War</a>, the U.S. Navy defended U.S. ships from the Barbary pirates, blockaded the Barbary ports and executed attacks against the Barbary' fleets.</p>
<p>The U.S. Navy saw substantial action in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, where it was victorious in eleven single-ship duels with the Royal Navy. It drove all significant British forces off <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Champlain" title="Lake Champlain">Lake Champlain</a> and prevented them from becoming British-controlled zones. The result was a major defeat for the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812#Niagara_Frontier.2C_1813" title="War of 1812">British invasion of New York state</a>, and the defeat of the military threat from the Native American allies of the British. Despite this, the U.S. Navy was unable to prevent the British from blockading its ports and landing troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-multiple1_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-multiple1-28">[28]</a></sup> After the war, the U.S. Navy again focused its attention on protecting American shipping assets, sending squadrons to the Caribbean, the Mediterranean where it participated in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Barbary_War" title="Second Barbary War">Second Barbary War</a> that ended piracy in the region, South America, Africa, and the Pacific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-love_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-love-20">[20]</a></sup> From 1819 to the outbreak of the Civil War, the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Squadron" title="Africa Squadron">Africa Squadron</a> operated to suppress the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a>, seizing 36 slave ships, although its contribution was smaller than that of the much larger British Royal Navy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Constitution_vs_Guerriere.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="509" data-file-width="740" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/USS_Constitution_vs_Guerriere.jpg/220px-USS_Constitution_vs_Guerriere.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/USS_Constitution_vs_Guerriere.jpg/330px-USS_Constitution_vs_Guerriere.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/USS_Constitution_vs_Guerriere.jpg/440px-USS_Constitution_vs_Guerriere.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Constitution_vs_Guerriere.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Constitution_vs_HMS_Guerriere" title="USS Constitution vs HMS Guerriere">USS <i>Constitution</i> vs HMS <i>Guerriere</i></a> during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a> the U.S. Navy blockaded Mexican ports, capturing or burning the Mexican fleet in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_California" title="Gulf of California">Gulf of California</a> and capturing all major cities in <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a> peninsula. In 1846–1848 the Navy successfully used the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Squadron" title="Pacific Squadron">Pacific Squadron</a> under Commodore <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Stockton" title="Robert Stockton">Robert Stockton</a> and its marines and blue-jackets to facilitate the capture of California with large scale land operations coordinated with the local militia organized in the <a href="/wiki/California_Battalion" title="California Battalion">California Battalion</a>. The Navy conducted the U.S. military's first large-scale amphibious joint operation by successfully landing 12,000 army troops with their equipment in one day at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veracruz,_Veracruz" title="Veracruz, Veracruz">Veracruz, Mexico</a>. When larger guns were needed to bombard Veracruz, Navy volunteers landed large guns and manned them in the successful bombardment and capture of the city. This successful landing and capture of Veracruz opened the way for the capture of Mexico City and the end of the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-multiple1_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-multiple1-28">[28]</a></sup> The U.S. Navy established itself as a player in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_foreign_policy" title="United States foreign policy">United States foreign policy</a> through the actions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commodore_(USN)" title="Commodore (USN)">Commodore</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matthew_Perry_(naval_officer)" title="Matthew Perry (naval officer)">Matthew Perry</a> in Japan, which resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Kanagawa" title="Convention of Kanagawa">Convention of Kanagawa</a> in 1854.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Naval power played a significant role during the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, in which the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a> had a distinct advantage over the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederacy</a> on the seas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-multiple1_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-multiple1-28">[28]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Union_blockade" title="Union blockade">Union blockade</a> on all major ports shut down exports and the coastal trade, but blockade runners (mostly owned and operated by British companies) provided a thin lifeline. The <a href="/wiki/Brown-water_navy" title="Brown-water navy">brown-water Navy's</a> control of the river systems made internal travel difficult for Confederates and easy for the Union. The war saw <a href="/wiki/Ironclad_warship" title="Ironclad warship">ironclad warships</a> in combat for the first time at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hampton_Roads" title="Battle of Hampton Roads">Battle of Hampton Roads</a> in 1862, which pitted <a href="/wiki/USS_Monitor" title="USS Monitor">USS <i>Monitor</i></a> against <a href="/wiki/CSS_Virginia" title="CSS Virginia">CSS <i>Virginia</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> For two decades after the war, however, the U.S. Navy's fleet was neglected and became technologically obsolete.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Us-atlantic-fleet-1907.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="464" data-file-width="738" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Us-atlantic-fleet-1907.jpg/220px-Us-atlantic-fleet-1907.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Us-atlantic-fleet-1907.jpg/330px-Us-atlantic-fleet-1907.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Us-atlantic-fleet-1907.jpg/440px-Us-atlantic-fleet-1907.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Us-atlantic-fleet-1907.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Great_White_Fleet" title="Great White Fleet">Great White Fleet</a> demonstrates U.S. naval power in 1907; it was proof that the U.S. Navy had <a href="/wiki/Blue-water_navy" title="Blue-water navy">blue-water capability</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Our ships are our natural bulwarks.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FamousNavyQuotes_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-FamousNavyQuotes-17">[17]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>A modernization program beginning in the 1880s when the first steel hulled warships stimulated the American steel industry, and "the new steel navy" was born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> This rapid expansion of the U.S. Navy and its easy victory over the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy" title="Spanish Navy">Spanish Navy</a> in 1898 brought a new respect for American technical quality. Rapid building of at first pre-dreadnoughts, then <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dreadnoughts" title="Dreadnoughts">dreadnoughts</a> brought the U.S. in line with the navies of countries such as <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. In 1907, most of the Navy's battleships, with several support vessels, dubbed the <a href="/wiki/Great_White_Fleet" title="Great White Fleet">Great White Fleet</a>, were showcased in a 14-month circumnavigation of the world. Ordered by President <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>, it was a mission designed to demonstrate the Navy's capability to extend to the global theater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-love_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-love-20">[20]</a></sup> By 1911, the U.S. had begun building the super-dreadnoughts at a pace to eventually become competitive with Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Puck_cover2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3461" data-file-width="2466" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Puck_cover2.jpg/170px-Puck_cover2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Puck_cover2.jpg/255px-Puck_cover2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Puck_cover2.jpg/340px-Puck_cover2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Puck_cover2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Columbia_(name)" title="Columbia (name)">Columbia</a>, personification of the United States, wearing a warship bearing the words "World Power" as her "Easter bonnet" on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Puck_(magazine)" title="Puck (magazine)">Puck</a></i>, 6 April 1901.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I_and_interwar_years">World War I and interwar years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: World War I and interwar years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The U.S. Navy saw little action during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. It concentrated on mine laying operations against German U-Boats. Hesitation by the senior command meant that naval forces were not contributed until late 1917. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Battleship_Division_Nine_(World_War_I)" title="United States Battleship Division Nine (World War I)">Battleship Division Nine</a> was dispatched to Britain and served as the Sixth Battle Squadron of the British Grand Fleet. Its presence allowed the British to decommission some older ships and reuse the crews on smaller vessels. Destroyers and U.S. Naval Air Force units contributed to the anti-submarine operations. The strength of the United States Navy grew under an ambitious ship building program associated with the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Act_of_1916" title="Naval Act of 1916">Naval Act of 1916</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Naval construction, especially of battleships was limited by the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Naval_Conference" title="Washington Naval Conference">Washington Naval Conference</a> of 1921–22. The aircraft carriers <a href="/wiki/USS_Saratoga_(CV-3)" title="USS Saratoga (CV-3)">USS <i>Saratoga</i> (CV-3)</a> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Lexington_(CV-2)" title="USS Lexington (CV-2)">USS <i>Lexington</i> (CV-2)</a> were built on the hulls of partially built battle cruisers that had been canceled by the treaty. The <a href="/wiki/New_Deal" title="New Deal">New Deal</a> used <a href="/wiki/Public_Works_Administration" title="Public Works Administration">Public Works Administration</a> funds to build warships, such as <a href="/wiki/USS_Yorktown_(CV-5)" title="USS Yorktown (CV-5)">USS <i>Yorktown</i> (CV-5)</a> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(CV-6)" title="USS Enterprise (CV-6)">USS <i>Enterprise</i> (CV-6)</a>. By 1936, with the completion of <a href="/wiki/USS_Wasp_(CV-7)" title="USS Wasp (CV-7)">USS <i>Wasp</i> (CV-7)</a>, the U.S. Navy possessed a carrier fleet of 165,000 tonnes <a href="/wiki/Displacement_(ship)" title="Displacement (ship)">displacement</a>, although this figure was nominally recorded as 135,000 tonnes to comply with treaty limitations. Franklin Roosevelt, the number two official in the Navy Department during World War I, appreciated the Navy and gave it strong support. In return, senior leaders were eager for innovation and experimented with new technologies, such as magnetic torpedoes, and developed a strategy called <a href="/wiki/War_Plan_Orange" title="War Plan Orange">War Plan Orange</a> for victory in the Pacific in a hypothetical war with Japan that would eventually become reality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_in_World_War_II" title="United States Navy in World War II">United States Navy in World War II</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Mexico_class_battleship_bombarding_Okinawa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4523" data-file-width="5730" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/New_Mexico_class_battleship_bombarding_Okinawa.jpg/170px-New_Mexico_class_battleship_bombarding_Okinawa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/New_Mexico_class_battleship_bombarding_Okinawa.jpg/255px-New_Mexico_class_battleship_bombarding_Okinawa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/New_Mexico_class_battleship_bombarding_Okinawa.jpg/340px-New_Mexico_class_battleship_bombarding_Okinawa.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Mexico_class_battleship_bombarding_Okinawa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The battleship <a href="/wiki/USS_Idaho_(BB-42)" title="USS Idaho (BB-42)">USS <i>Idaho</i></a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Okinawa" title="Battle of Okinawa">shells Okinawa</a> on 1 April 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The U.S. Navy grew into a formidable force in the years prior to <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, with battleship production being restarted in 1937, commencing with <a href="/wiki/USS_North_Carolina_(BB-55)" title="USS North Carolina (BB-55)">USS <i>North Carolina</i> (BB-55)</a>. Though ultimately unsuccessful, Japan attempted to neutralize this strategic threat with the surprise <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a> on 7 December 1941. Following American entry into the war, the U.S. Navy grew tremendously as the United States was faced with a two-front war on the seas. It achieved notable acclaim in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific Theater</a>, where it was instrumental to the Allies' successful "<a href="/wiki/Leapfrogging_(strategy)" title="Leapfrogging (strategy)">island hopping</a>" campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-howarth_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-howarth-21">[21]</a></sup> The U.S. Navy participated in many significant battles, including the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea" title="Battle of the Coral Sea">Battle of the Coral Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">Battle of Midway</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_Campaign" title="Solomon Islands Campaign">Solomon Islands Campaign</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Philippine_Sea" title="Battle of the Philippine Sea">Battle of the Philippine Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leyte_Gulf" title="Battle of Leyte Gulf">Battle of Leyte Gulf</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Okinawa" title="Battle of Okinawa">Battle of Okinawa</a>. By war's end in 1945, the U.S. Navy had added hundreds of new ships, including 18 aircraft carriers and 8 battleships, and had over 70% of the world's total numbers and total tonnage of naval vessels of 1,000 tons or greater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Defense_Analysis.3B_Dec_2001.2C_Vol._17_Issue_3.2C_p._259.E2.80.93265_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Defense_Analysis.3B_Dec_2001.2C_Vol._17_Issue_3.2C_p._259.E2.80.93265-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> At its peak, the U.S. Navy was operating 6,768 ships on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V-J_Day" title="V-J Day">V-J Day</a> in August 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Doctrine had significantly shifted by the end of the war. The U.S. Navy had followed in the footsteps of the navies of Great Britain and Germany which favored concentrated groups of battleships as their main offensive naval weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The development of the aircraft carrier and its devastating utilization by the Japanese against the U.S. at Pearl Harbor, however, shifted U.S. thinking. The Pearl Harbor attack destroyed or took out of action a significant number of U.S. Navy battleships. This placed much of the burden of retaliating against the Japanese on the small number of aircraft carriers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War">Cold War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cold War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_George_Washington_(SSBN-598).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1267" data-file-width="2100" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/USS_George_Washington_%28SSBN-598%29.jpg/220px-USS_George_Washington_%28SSBN-598%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/USS_George_Washington_%28SSBN-598%29.jpg/330px-USS_George_Washington_%28SSBN-598%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/USS_George_Washington_%28SSBN-598%29.jpg/440px-USS_George_Washington_%28SSBN-598%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_George_Washington_(SSBN-598).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_George_Washington_(SSBN-598)" title="USS George Washington (SSBN-598)">USS <i>George Washington</i> (SSBN-598)</a>, a ballistic missile submarine</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The potential for armed conflict with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> pushed the U.S. Navy to continue its technological advancement by developing new weapons systems, ships, and aircraft. U.S. naval strategy changed to that of forward deployment in support of U.S. allies with an emphasis on carrier battle groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>The navy was a major participant in the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, blockaded Cuba during the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a>, and, through the use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile_submarines" title="Ballistic missile submarines">ballistic missile submarines</a>, became an important aspect of the United States' <a href="/wiki/Mutual_assured_destruction" title="Mutual assured destruction">nuclear strategic deterrence</a> policy. The U.S. Navy conducted various combat operations in the Persian Gulf against Iran in 1987 and 1988, most notably <a href="/wiki/Operation_Praying_Mantis" title="Operation Praying Mantis">Operation Praying Mantis</a>. The Navy was extensively involved in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Urgent_Fury" title="Operation Urgent Fury">Operation Urgent Fury</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Desert_Shield_(Gulf_War)" title="Operation Desert Shield (Gulf War)">Operation Desert Shield</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Desert_Storm" title="Operation Desert Storm">Operation Desert Storm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Deliberate_Force" title="Operation Deliberate Force">Operation Deliberate Force</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Allied_Force" title="Operation Allied Force">Operation Allied Force</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Desert_Fox" title="Operation Desert Fox">Operation Desert Fox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Southern_Watch" title="Operation Southern Watch">Operation Southern Watch</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The U.S. Navy has also been involved in search and rescue/search and salvage operations, sometimes in conjunction with vessels of other countries as well as with U.S. Coast Guard ships. Two examples are the <a href="/wiki/1966_Palomares_B-52_crash" title="1966 Palomares B-52 crash">1966 Palomares B-52 crash</a> incident and search for the nuclear bombs, and Task Force 71 of the Seventh Fleet operation in search for <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air_Lines_Flight_007" title="Korean Air Lines Flight 007">Korean Air Lines Flight 007</a> shot down by the Soviets on 1 September 1983.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>When a crisis confronts the nation, the first question often asked by policymakers is: 'What naval forces are available and how fast can they be on station?'</p>
<div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>Admiral <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carlisle_A._H._Trost" title="Carlisle A. H. Trost">Carlisle A. H. Trost</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>The U.S. Navy continues to be a major support to U.S. interests in the 21st century. Since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, it has shifted its focus from preparations for large-scale war with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> to special operations and strike missions in regional conflicts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forward_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-forward-40">[40]</a></sup> The navy participated in <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">Operation Enduring Freedom</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Iraqi_Freedom" title="Operation Iraqi Freedom">Operation Iraqi Freedom</a>, and is a major participant in the ongoing <a href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" title="War on Terror">War on Terror</a>, largely in this capacity. Development continues on new ships and weapons, including the <a href="/wiki/Gerald_R._Ford-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Gerald R. Ford-class aircraft carrier"><i>Gerald R. Ford</i>-class</a> aircraft carrier and the <a href="/wiki/Littoral_combat_ship" title="Littoral combat ship">Littoral combat ship</a>. Because of its size, weapons technology, and ability to project force far from U.S. shores, the current U.S. Navy remains a potent asset for the United States. Moreover, it is the principal means through which the U.S. maintains international global order, namely by safeguarding global trade and protecting allied nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, the U.S. Navy joined with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Marine_Corps" title="U.S. Marine Corps">U.S. Marine Corps</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Coast_Guard" title="U.S. Coast Guard">U.S. Coast Guard</a> to adopt a new maritime strategy called <a href="/wiki/A_Cooperative_Strategy_for_21st_Century_Seapower" title="A Cooperative Strategy for 21st Century Seapower">A Cooperative Strategy for 21st Century Seapower</a> that raises the notion of prevention of war to the same philosophical level as the conduct of war. The strategy was presented by the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Naval_Operations" title="Chief of Naval Operations">Chief of Naval Operations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commandant_of_the_Marine_Corps" title="Commandant of the Marine Corps">Commandant of the Marine Corps</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Commandant_of_the_Coast_Guard" title="Commandant of the Coast Guard">Commandant of the Coast Guard</a> at the International Sea Power Symposium in <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport, RI</a> on 17 October 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The strategy recognized the economic links of the global system and how any disruption due to regional crises—man-made or natural—can adversely impact the U.S. economy and quality of life. This new strategy charts a course for the Navy, Coast Guard, and Marine Corps to work collectively with each other and international partners to prevent these crises from occurring or reacting quickly should one occur to prevent negative impacts on the U.S.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 2010, Chief of Naval Operations, Admiral Gary Roughead, noted that demands on the Navy have grown as the fleet has shrunk and that in the face of declining budgets in the future, the U.S. Navy must rely even more on international partnerships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In its 2013 budget request, the navy focused on retaining all eleven big deck carriers, at the expense of cutting numbers of smaller ships and delaying the SSBN replacement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> By the next year the USN found itself unable to maintain eleven aircraft carriers in the face of the expiration of budget relief offered by the <a href="/wiki/Bipartisan_Budget_Act_of_2013" title="Bipartisan Budget Act of 2013">Bipartisan Budget Act of 2013</a> and CNO <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Greenert" title="Jonathan Greenert">Jonathan Greenert</a> said that a ten ship carrier fleet would not be able to sustainably support military requirements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The British <a href="/wiki/First_Sea_Lord" title="First Sea Lord">First Sea Lord</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Zambellas" title="George Zambellas">George Zambellas</a> said that <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thediplomat1_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-thediplomat1-46">[46]</a></sup> the USN had switched from "outcome-led to resource-led" planning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>One significant change in U.S. policymaking that is having a major effect on naval planning is the <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_foreign_policy_of_the_Barack_Obama_administration" title="East Asian foreign policy of the Barack Obama administration">Pivot to East Asia</a>. In response this, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="Secretary of the Navy">Secretary of the Navy</a> <a href="/wiki/Ray_Mabus" title="Ray Mabus">Ray Mabus</a> has stated that 60 percent of the total U.S. fleet will be deployed to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> by the year 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The Navy's most recent 30-year shipbuilding plan, published in 2016, calls for a future fleet of 350 ships in order to meet the challenges of an increasingly competitive international environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thediplomat1_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-thediplomat1-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Structure_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Structure of the United States Navy">Structure of the United States Navy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_organization.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="617" data-file-width="655" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/US_Navy_organization.svg/250px-US_Navy_organization.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/US_Navy_organization.svg/375px-US_Navy_organization.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/US_Navy_organization.svg/500px-US_Navy_organization.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_organization.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Simplified flowchart of U.S. Navy command structure</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The U.S. Navy falls under the administration of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Navy" title="United States Department of the Navy">Department of the Navy</a>, under civilian leadership of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="United States Secretary of the Navy">Secretary of the Navy (SECNAV)</a>. The most senior naval officer is the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Naval_Operations" title="Chief of Naval Operations">Chief of Naval Operations (CNO)</a>, a four-star admiral who is immediately under and reports to the Secretary of the Navy. At the same time, the Chief of Naval Operations is one of the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Joint Chiefs of Staff">Joint Chiefs of Staff</a>, which is the second-highest deliberatory body of the armed forces after the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Security_Council" title="United States National Security Council">United States National Security Council</a>, although it only plays an advisory role to the President and does not nominally form part of the chain of command. The Secretary of the Navy and Chief of Naval Operations are responsible for organizing, recruiting, training, and equipping the Navy so that it is ready for operation under the command of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unified_Combatant_Command" title="Unified Combatant Command">unified combat command commanders</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operating_forces">Operating forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Operating forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_units_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="List of units of the United States Navy">List of units of the United States Navy</a></div>
<p>There are nine components in the operating forces of the U.S. Navy: the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fleet_Forces_Command" title="United States Fleet Forces Command">United States Fleet Forces Command</a> (formerly United States Atlantic Fleet), <a href="/wiki/United_States_Pacific_Fleet" title="United States Pacific Fleet">United States Pacific Fleet</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Forces_Central_Command" title="United States Naval Forces Central Command">United States Naval Forces Central Command</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Forces_Europe" title="United States Naval Forces Europe">United States Naval Forces Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naval_Network_Warfare_Command" title="Naval Network Warfare Command">Naval Network Warfare Command</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_Reserve" title="United States Navy Reserve">Navy Reserve</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Special_Warfare_Command" title="United States Naval Special Warfare Command">United States Naval Special Warfare Command</a>, <a href="/wiki/Operational_Test_and_Evaluation_Force" title="Operational Test and Evaluation Force">Operational Test and Evaluation Force</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Military_Sealift_Command" title="Military Sealift Command">Military Sealift Command</a>. Fleet Forces Command controls a number of unique capabilities, including Military Sealift Command, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Expeditionary_Combat_Command" title="Naval Expeditionary Combat Command">Naval Expeditionary Combat Command</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Navy_Cyber_Forces" title="Navy Cyber Forces">Navy Cyber Forces</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The United States Navy has six active numbered fleets – <a href="/wiki/United_States_Third_Fleet" title="United States Third Fleet">Third</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fifth_Fleet" title="United States Fifth Fleet">Fifth</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Sixth_Fleet" title="United States Sixth Fleet">Sixth</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Seventh_Fleet" title="United States Seventh Fleet">Seventh Fleet</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Tenth_Fleet" title="United States Tenth Fleet">Tenth Fleets</a> are each led by a <a href="/wiki/Vice_admiral_(United_States)" title="Vice admiral (United States)">vice admiral</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fourth_Fleet" title="United States Fourth Fleet">Fourth Fleet</a> is led by a <a href="/wiki/Rear_admiral_(United_States)" title="Rear admiral (United States)">rear admiral</a>. These six fleets are further grouped under Fleet Forces Command (the former Atlantic Fleet), Pacific Fleet, Naval Forces Europe-Africa, and Naval Forces Central Command, whose commander also doubles as Commander Fifth Fleet; the first three commands being led by four-star admirals. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_First_Fleet" title="United States First Fleet">United States First Fleet</a> existed after the Second World War from 1947, but it was redesignated the Third Fleet in early 1973. In early 2008, the navy reactivated the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fourth_Fleet" title="United States Fourth Fleet">United States Fourth Fleet</a> to control operations in the area controlled by Southern Command, which consists of US assets in and around Central and South America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shore_establishments">Shore establishments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Shore establishments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Kitty_Hawk_at_Yokosuka.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/USS_Kitty_Hawk_at_Yokosuka.jpg/220px-USS_Kitty_Hawk_at_Yokosuka.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/USS_Kitty_Hawk_at_Yokosuka.jpg/330px-USS_Kitty_Hawk_at_Yokosuka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/USS_Kitty_Hawk_at_Yokosuka.jpg/440px-USS_Kitty_Hawk_at_Yokosuka.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Kitty_Hawk_at_Yokosuka.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Kitty_Hawk_(CV-63)" title="USS Kitty Hawk (CV-63)">USS <i>Kitty Hawk</i> (CV-63)</a> docks at the U.S. Navy base in <a href="/wiki/Yokosuka,_Kanagawa" title="Yokosuka, Kanagawa">Yokosuka, Japan</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Shore establishments exist to support the mission of the fleet through the use of facilities on land. Among the commands of the shore establishment, as of April 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, are the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Education_and_Training_Command" title="Naval Education and Training Command">Naval Education and Training Command</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commander,_Naval_Meteorology_and_Oceanography_Command" title="Commander, Naval Meteorology and Oceanography Command">Naval Meteorology and Oceanography Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Space_and_Naval_Warfare_Systems_Command" title="Space and Naval Warfare Systems Command">Space and Naval Warfare Systems Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Facilities_Engineering_Command" title="Naval Facilities Engineering Command">Naval Facilities Engineering Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Supply_Systems_Command" title="Naval Supply Systems Command">Naval Supply Systems Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Systems_Command" title="Naval Air Systems Command">Naval Air Systems Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Sea_Systems_Command" title="Naval Sea Systems Command">Naval Sea Systems Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Medicine_and_Surgery" title="Bureau of Medicine and Surgery">Bureau of Medicine and Surgery</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Naval_Personnel" title="Bureau of Naval Personnel">Bureau of Naval Personnel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">United States Naval Academy</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Safety_Center" title="Naval Safety Center">Naval Safety Center</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Strike_and_Air_Warfare_Center" title="Naval Strike and Air Warfare Center">Naval Strike and Air Warfare Center</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Observatory" title="United States Naval Observatory">United States Naval Observatory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Official Navy websites list the Office of the Chief of Naval Operations and the chief of naval operations as part of the shore establishment, but these two entities effectively sit superior to the other organizations, playing a coordinating role.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships_with_other_service_branches">Relationships with other service branches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Relationships with other service branches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_Marine_Corps">United States Marine Corps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: United States Marine Corps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:F-18A_Hornet_VMFA-451_USS_Coral_Sea_1989.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1860" data-file-width="2840" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/F-18A_Hornet_VMFA-451_USS_Coral_Sea_1989.jpeg/220px-F-18A_Hornet_VMFA-451_USS_Coral_Sea_1989.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/F-18A_Hornet_VMFA-451_USS_Coral_Sea_1989.jpeg/330px-F-18A_Hornet_VMFA-451_USS_Coral_Sea_1989.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/F-18A_Hornet_VMFA-451_USS_Coral_Sea_1989.jpeg/440px-F-18A_Hornet_VMFA-451_USS_Coral_Sea_1989.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:F-18A_Hornet_VMFA-451_USS_Coral_Sea_1989.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">Marine</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F/A-18" title="F/A-18">F/A-18</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VMFA-451" title="VMFA-451">VMFA-451</a> prepares to launch from <a href="/wiki/USS_Coral_Sea_(CV-43)" title="USS Coral Sea (CV-43)">USS <i>Coral Sea</i> (CV-43)</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a></div>
<p>In 1834, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a> came under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_the_Navy" title="Department of the Navy">Department of the Navy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Historically, the Navy has had a unique relationship with the USMC, partly because they both specialize in seaborne operations. Together the Navy and Marine Corps form the Department of the Navy and report to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="United States Secretary of the Navy">Secretary of the Navy</a>. However, the Marine Corps is a distinct, separate service branch<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSA1947sec606_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-NSA1947sec606-52">[52]</a></sup> with its own uniformed service chief – the Commandant of the Marine Corps, a four-star general.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The Marine Corps depends on the Navy for medical support (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dentists" title="Dentists">dentists</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_doctor" title="Medical doctor">doctors</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nurse" title="Nurse">nurses</a>, medical technicians known as <a href="/wiki/Hospital_corpsman" title="Hospital corpsman">corpsmen</a>) and religious support (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chaplains" title="Chaplains">chaplains</a>). Thus Navy officers and enlisted sailors fulfill these roles. When attached to Marine Corps units deployed to an operational environment they generally wear Marine camouflage uniforms, but otherwise they wear Navy <a href="/wiki/Dress_uniform" title="Dress uniform">dress uniforms</a> unless they opt to conform to Marine Corps grooming standards.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the operational environment, as an expeditionary force specializing in amphibious operations, Marines often embark on Navy ships to conduct operations from beyond territorial waters. Marine units deploying as part of a Marine Air-Ground Task Force (MAGTF) operate under the command of the existing Marine chain of command. Although Marine units routinely operate from amphibious assault ships, the relationship has evolved over the years much as the Commander of the Carrier Air Group/Wing (CAG) does not work for the carrier commanding officer, but coordinates with the ship's CO and staff. Some Marine aviation squadrons, usually fixed-wing assigned to carrier air wings train and operate alongside Navy squadrons; they fly similar missions and often fly sorties together under the cognizance of the CAG. Aviation is where the Navy and Marines share the most common ground, since aircrews are guided in their use of aircraft by standard procedures outlined in series of publications known as <a href="/wiki/NATOPS" title="NATOPS">NATOPS</a> manuals.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_Coast_Guard">United States Coast Guard</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: United States Coast Guard">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Official_U.S._Navy_Imagery_-_U.S._Coast_Guard_helicopters_land_aboard_USS_Wasp..jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2340" data-file-width="3827" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Flickr_-_Official_U.S._Navy_Imagery_-_U.S._Coast_Guard_helicopters_land_aboard_USS_Wasp..jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Official_U.S._Navy_Imagery_-_U.S._Coast_Guard_helicopters_land_aboard_USS_Wasp..jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Flickr_-_Official_U.S._Navy_Imagery_-_U.S._Coast_Guard_helicopters_land_aboard_USS_Wasp..jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Official_U.S._Navy_Imagery_-_U.S._Coast_Guard_helicopters_land_aboard_USS_Wasp..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Flickr_-_Official_U.S._Navy_Imagery_-_U.S._Coast_Guard_helicopters_land_aboard_USS_Wasp..jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Official_U.S._Navy_Imagery_-_U.S._Coast_Guard_helicopters_land_aboard_USS_Wasp..jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Official_U.S._Navy_Imagery_-_U.S._Coast_Guard_helicopters_land_aboard_USS_Wasp..jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A U.S. Coast Guard helicopter prepares to land on the flight deck of the amphibious assault ship <a href="/wiki/USS_Wasp_(LHD-1)" title="USS Wasp (LHD-1)">USS <i>Wasp</i> (LHD-1)</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">United States Coast Guard</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">United States Coast Guard</a>, in its peacetime role with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a>, fulfills its law enforcement and rescue role in the maritime environment. It provides <a href="/wiki/Law_Enforcement_Detachments" title="Law Enforcement Detachments">Law Enforcement Detachments</a> (LEDETs) to Navy vessels, where they perform arrests and other law enforcement duties during naval boarding and interdiction missions. In times of war, the Coast Guard operates as a service in the Navy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> At other times, Coast Guard <a href="/wiki/Port_Security_Unit" title="Port Security Unit">port security units</a> are sent overseas to guard the security of ports and other assets. The Coast Guard also jointly staffs the Navy's naval coastal warfare groups and squadrons (the latter of which were known as harbor defense commands until late-2004), which oversee defense efforts in foreign littoral combat and inshore areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">Personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Personnel_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Personnel of the United States Navy">Personnel of the United States Navy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_SEALs_at_Zhawar_Kili_cave_entrance.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/US_Navy_SEALs_at_Zhawar_Kili_cave_entrance.jpg/220px-US_Navy_SEALs_at_Zhawar_Kili_cave_entrance.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/US_Navy_SEALs_at_Zhawar_Kili_cave_entrance.jpg/330px-US_Navy_SEALs_at_Zhawar_Kili_cave_entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/US_Navy_SEALs_at_Zhawar_Kili_cave_entrance.jpg/440px-US_Navy_SEALs_at_Zhawar_Kili_cave_entrance.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_SEALs_at_Zhawar_Kili_cave_entrance.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_SEALs" title="United States Navy SEALs">Navy SEALs</a> at one of the entrances <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhawar_Kili" title="Zhawar Kili">Zhawar Kili</a> cave complex.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The United States Navy has nearly 500,000 personnel, approximately a quarter of whom are in ready reserve. Of those on active duty, more than eighty percent are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enlisted" title="Enlisted">enlisted</a> sailors, and around fifteen percent are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commissioned_officer" title="Commissioned officer">commissioned officers</a>; the rest are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Midshipmen" title="Midshipmen">midshipmen</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">United States Naval Academy</a> and midshipmen of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Reserve_Officer_Training_Corps" title="Naval Reserve Officer Training Corps">Naval Reserve Officer Training Corps</a> at over 180 universities around the country and officer candidates at the Navy's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Officer_Candidate_School_(U.S._Navy)" title="Officer Candidate School (U.S. Navy)">Officer Candidate School</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-status-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Enlisted sailors complete basic military training at <a href="/wiki/Recruit_Training_Command,_Great_Lakes,_Illinois" title="Recruit Training Command, Great Lakes, Illinois">boot camp</a> and then are sent to complete training for their individual <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Navy_ratings" title="List of United States Navy ratings">careers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sailors prove they have mastered skills and deserve responsibilities by completing Personnel Qualification Standards (PQS) tasks and examinations. Among the most important is the "warfare qualification", which denotes a journeyman level of capability in Surface Warfare, Aviation Warfare, Information Dominance Warfare, Naval Aircrew, Special Warfare, Seabee Warfare, Submarine Warfare or Expeditionary Warfare. Many qualifications are denoted on a sailor's uniform with <a href="/wiki/Badges_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Badges of the United States Navy">U.S. Navy badges and insignia</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniforms">Uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Uniforms_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Uniforms of the United States Navy">Uniforms of the United States Navy</a></div>
<p>The uniforms of the U.S. Navy have evolved gradually since the first uniform regulations for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Officer_(military)" title="Officer (military)">officers</a> were issued in 1802 on the formation of the Navy Department. The predominant colors of U.S. Navy uniforms are <a href="/wiki/Navy_blue" title="Navy blue">navy blue</a> and <a href="/wiki/White" title="White">white</a>. U.S. Navy uniforms were based on <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> uniforms of the time, and have tended to follow that template.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commissioned_officers">Commissioned officers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Commissioned officers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_officer_rank_insignia" title="United States Navy officer rank insignia">United States Navy officer rank insignia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ranks_and_insignia_of_NATO_navies_officers" title="Ranks and insignia of NATO navies officers">Ranks and insignia of NATO navies officers</a></div>
<p>The commissioned officer ranks of the U.S. Navy are divided into three categories: <a href="/wiki/Junior_officer" title="Junior officer">junior officers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_rank#Field_or_senior_officers" title="Military rank">senior officers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Flag_officer" title="Flag officer">flag officers</a>. Junior officers are those officers in pay grades O-1 to O-4, while senior officers are those in pay grades O-5 and O-6, and flag officers are those in pay grades of O-7 and above.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Enlisted">Enlisted</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Enlisted">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Navy_enlisted_rates" title="List of United States Navy enlisted rates">List of United States Navy enlisted rates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ranks_and_insignia_of_NATO_navies_enlisted" title="Ranks and insignia of NATO navies enlisted">Ranks and insignia of NATO navies enlisted</a></div>
<p>Sailors in pay grades E-1 through E-3 are considered to be in apprenticeships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAVYDAT2_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAVYDAT2-57">[57]</a></sup> They are divided into five definable groups, with colored group rate marks designating the group to which they belong: Seaman/Seawoman, Fireman, Airman, Constructionman, and Hospitalman. <b>E-4</b> to <b>E-6</b> are <a href="/wiki/Non-commissioned_officer" title="Non-commissioned officer">non-commissioned officers</a> (NCOs), and are specifically called <a href="/wiki/Petty_officer" title="Petty officer">Petty Officers</a> in the Navy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BUPERS_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-BUPERS-58">[58]</a></sup> Petty Officers perform not only the duties of their specific career field but also serve as leaders to junior enlisted personnel. E-7 to E-9 are still considered Petty Officers, but are considered a separate community within the Navy. They have separate berthing and dining facilities (where feasible), wear separate uniforms, and perform separate duties.</p>
<p>After attaining the rate of Master Chief Petty Officer, a service member may choose to further his or her career by becoming a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Command_Master_Chief_Petty_Officer" title="Command Master Chief Petty Officer">Command Master Chief Petty Officer</a> (CMC). A CMC is considered to be the senior-most enlisted service member within a command, and is the special assistant to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commanding_Officer" title="Commanding Officer">Commanding Officer</a> in all matters pertaining to the health, welfare, job satisfaction, morale, utilization, advancement and training of the command's enlisted personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MILCMDMC_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-MILCMDMC-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPUBCMC_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-IPUBCMC-60">[60]</a></sup> CMCs can be Command level (within a single unit, such as a ship or shore station), Fleet level (squadrons consisting of multiple operational units, headed by a flag officer or commodore), or Force level (consisting of a separate community within the Navy, such as Subsurface, Air, Reserves).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OPNAV1306_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-OPNAV1306-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>CMC insignia are similar to the insignia for Master Chief, except that the rating symbol is replaced by an inverted five-point star, reflecting a change in their rating from their previous rating (i.e., MMCM) to CMDCM. The stars for Command Master Chief are silver, while stars for Fleet or Force Master Chief are gold. Additionally, CMCs wear a badge, worn on their left breast pocket, denoting their title (Command/Fleet/Force).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPUBCMC_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-IPUBCMC-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BUPERSCPO_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-BUPERSCPO-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
