<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Badges_of_the_United_States_Navy">Badges of the United States Navy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Badges of the United States Navy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Badges_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Badges of the United States Navy">Badges of the United States Navy</a></div>
<p><b>Insignia and badges of the United States Navy</b> are military "badges" issued by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Navy" title="United States Department of the Navy">United States Department of the Navy</a> to naval service members who achieve certain qualifications and accomplishments while serving on both active and reserve duty in the United States Navy. Most naval aviation insignia are also permitted for wear on uniforms of the <a href="/wiki/Badges_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps" title="Badges of the United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a>.</p>
<p>As described in Chapter 5 of U.S. Navy Uniform Regulations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-navy_reg_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-navy_reg-63">[63]</a></sup> "badges" are categorized as <i>breast insignia</i> (usually worn immediately above and below ribbons) and <i>identification badges</i> (usually worn at breast pocket level).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chapter_5_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-chapter_5-64">[64]</a></sup> Breast insignia are further divided between <i>command</i> and <i>warfare and other qualification</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-section_2_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-section_2-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Insignia come in the form of metal "pin-on devices" worn on formal uniforms and embroidered "tape strips" worn on work uniforms. For the purpose of this article, the general term "insignia" shall be used to describe both, as it is done in Navy Uniform Regulations. The term "badge", although used ambiguously in other military branches and in informal speak to describe any pin, patch, or tab, is exclusive to <i>identification badges</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-article_5201.2_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-article_5201.2-66">[66]</a></sup> and authorized <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distinguished_Shot_Badge" title="Distinguished Shot Badge">marksmanship awards</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-article_5310_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-article_5310-67">[67]</a></sup> according to the language in Navy Uniform Regulations, Chapter 5. Below are just a few of the many badges maintained by the Navy. The rest can be seen in the article cited at the top of this section:</p>
<center>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bases">Bases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Bases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Navy_installations" title="List of United States Navy installations">List of United States Navy installations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_States_Navy_bases.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="593" data-file-width="959" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/United_States_Navy_bases.svg/300px-United_States_Navy_bases.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/United_States_Navy_bases.svg/450px-United_States_Navy_bases.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/United_States_Navy_bases.svg/600px-United_States_Navy_bases.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_States_Navy_bases.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Navy bases in the United States</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The size, complexity, and international presence of the United States Navy requires a large number of navy installations to support its operations. While the majority of bases are located inside the United States itself, the navy maintains a significant number of facilities abroad, either in U.S.-controlled territories or in foreign countries under a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Status_of_Forces_Agreement" title="Status of Forces Agreement">Status of Forces Agreement</a> (SOFA).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_United_States">Eastern United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Eastern United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The second largest concentration of installations is at <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, where the navy occupies over 36,000 acres (15,000 ha) of land. Located at Hampton Roads are <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Norfolk" title="Naval Station Norfolk">Naval Station Norfolk</a>, homeport of the Atlantic Fleet; <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Oceana" title="Naval Air Station Oceana">Naval Air Station Oceana</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Master_Jet_Base" title="Master Jet Base">Master Jet Base</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Amphibious_Base_Little_Creek" title="Naval Amphibious Base Little Creek">Naval Amphibious Base Little Creek</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Training_Support_Center_Hampton_Roads" title="Training Support Center Hampton Roads">Training Support Center Hampton Roads</a> as well as a number of Navy and commercial shipyards that service navy vessels. The Aegis Training and Readiness Center is located at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Support_Activity_South_Potomac" title="Naval Support Activity South Potomac">Naval Support Activity South Potomac</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dahlgren,_Virginia" title="Dahlgren, Virginia">Dahlgren, Virginia</a>. Maryland is home to <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Patuxent_River" title="Naval Air Station Patuxent River">NAS Patuxent River</a>, which houses the Navy's <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Test_Pilot_School" title="United States Naval Test Pilot School">Test Pilot School</a>. Also located in Maryland is the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">United States Naval Academy</a>, situated in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annapolis" title="Annapolis">Annapolis</a>. <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Newport" title="Naval Station Newport">NS Newport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport, Rhode Island</a> is home to many schools and tenant commands, including the <a href="/wiki/Officer_Candidate_School" title="Officer Candidate School">Officer Candidate School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naval_Undersea_Warfare_Center" title="Naval Undersea Warfare Center">Naval Undersea Warfare Center</a>, and more, and also maintains inactive ships.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>There is also a naval base in Charleston, South Carolina. This is home to the Nuclear A-School, and the Nuclear Field Power school, and one of two nuclear 'Prototype' Schools. The state of Florida is the location of three major bases, <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Mayport" title="Naval Station Mayport">NS Mayport</a>, the Navy's fourth largest, in <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville, Florida</a>; <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Jacksonville" title="Naval Air Station Jacksonville">NAS Jacksonville</a>, a Master Air Anti-submarine Warfare base; and <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Pensacola" title="Naval Air Station Pensacola">NAS Pensacola</a>; home of the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Education_and_Training_Command" title="Naval Education and Training Command">Naval Education and Training Command</a>, the Naval Air Technical Training Center that provides specialty training for enlisted aviation personnel and is the primary flight training base for Navy and Marine Corps <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Flight_Officer" title="Naval Flight Officer">Naval Flight Officers</a> and enlisted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Aircrewman" title="Naval Aircrewman">Naval Aircrewmen</a>. There is also <a href="/wiki/Naval_Support_Activity_Panama_City" title="Naval Support Activity Panama City">NSA Panama City</a>, Florida which is home to the Navy Diving and Salvage Training Center.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The main U.S. Navy <a href="/wiki/Submarine_base" title="Submarine base">submarine bases</a> on the east coast are located in <a href="/wiki/Naval_Submarine_Base_New_London" title="Naval Submarine Base New London">Naval Submarine Base New London</a> in <a href="/wiki/Groton,_Connecticut" title="Groton, Connecticut">Groton, Connecticut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naval_Submarine_Base_Kings_Bay" title="Naval Submarine Base Kings Bay">NSB Kings Bay</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kings_Bay,_Georgia" title="Kings Bay, Georgia">Kings Bay, Georgia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Naval_Shipyard" title="Portsmouth Naval Shipyard">Portsmouth Naval Shipyard</a> near <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_New_Hampshire" title="Portsmouth, New Hampshire">Portsmouth, New Hampshire</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> which repairs naval submarines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_2-6"><a href="#cite_note-status-2">[2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Great_Lakes" title="Naval Station Great Lakes">NS Great Lakes</a>, north of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" title="Chicago, Illinois">Chicago, Illinois</a> is the home of the Navy's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_Recruit_Training" title="United States Navy Recruit Training">boot camp</a> for enlisted sailors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Navy_Yard" title="Washington Navy Yard">Washington Navy Yard</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington,_DC" title="Washington, DC">Washington, DC</a> is the Navy's oldest shore establishment and serves as a ceremonial and administrative center for the U.S. Navy, home to the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Naval_Operations" title="Chief of Naval Operations">Chief of Naval Operations</a>, and is headquarters for numerous commands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_United_States_and_Hawaii">Western United States and Hawaii</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Western United States and Hawaii">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_SEALs_SEAL_jumps_over_side_boat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="330" data-file-width="500" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/US_Navy_SEALs_SEAL_jumps_over_side_boat.jpg/220px-US_Navy_SEALs_SEAL_jumps_over_side_boat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/US_Navy_SEALs_SEAL_jumps_over_side_boat.jpg/330px-US_Navy_SEALs_SEAL_jumps_over_side_boat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/US_Navy_SEALs_SEAL_jumps_over_side_boat.jpg/440px-US_Navy_SEALs_SEAL_jumps_over_side_boat.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_SEALs_SEAL_jumps_over_side_boat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Underwater_Demolition_Team" title="Underwater Demolition Team">Underwater Demolition Team</a> members using the casting technique from a speeding boat.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_120209-N-XD935-302_Mass_Communication_Specialist_1st_Class_Shane_Tuck,_assigned_to_the_Expeditionary_Combat_Camera_Underwater_Photo_Team,_c.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1848" data-file-width="2784" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/US_Navy_120209-N-XD935-302_Mass_Communication_Specialist_1st_Class_Shane_Tuck%2C_assigned_to_the_Expeditionary_Combat_Camera_Underwater_Photo_Team%2C_c.jpg/220px-US_Navy_120209-N-XD935-302_Mass_Communication_Specialist_1st_Class_Shane_Tuck%2C_assigned_to_the_Expeditionary_Combat_Camera_Underwater_Photo_Team%2C_c.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/US_Navy_120209-N-XD935-302_Mass_Communication_Specialist_1st_Class_Shane_Tuck%2C_assigned_to_the_Expeditionary_Combat_Camera_Underwater_Photo_Team%2C_c.jpg/330px-US_Navy_120209-N-XD935-302_Mass_Communication_Specialist_1st_Class_Shane_Tuck%2C_assigned_to_the_Expeditionary_Combat_Camera_Underwater_Photo_Team%2C_c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/US_Navy_120209-N-XD935-302_Mass_Communication_Specialist_1st_Class_Shane_Tuck%2C_assigned_to_the_Expeditionary_Combat_Camera_Underwater_Photo_Team%2C_c.jpg/440px-US_Navy_120209-N-XD935-302_Mass_Communication_Specialist_1st_Class_Shane_Tuck%2C_assigned_to_the_Expeditionary_Combat_Camera_Underwater_Photo_Team%2C_c.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_120209-N-XD935-302_Mass_Communication_Specialist_1st_Class_Shane_Tuck,_assigned_to_the_Expeditionary_Combat_Camera_Underwater_Photo_Team,_c.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Combat Camera Underwater Photo Team – A US Navy diver during <a href="/wiki/Underwater_photography" title="Underwater photography">underwater photography</a> training off the coast of Guantanamo Bay.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The navy's largest complex is <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Weapons_Station_China_Lake" title="Naval Air Weapons Station China Lake">Naval Air Weapons Station China Lake</a>, California, which covers 1.1 million acres (4,500 km<sup>2</sup>) of land, or approximately 1/3 of the United States Navy's total land holdings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_2-7"><a href="#cite_note-status-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Naval_Base_San_Diego" title="Naval Base San Diego">Naval Base San Diego</a>, California, is the main homeport of the Pacific Fleet (although its headquarters is located in <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>, Hawaii). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAS_North_Island" title="NAS North Island">NAS North Island</a> is located on the north side of <a href="/wiki/Coronado,_California" title="Coronado, California">Coronado</a>, and is home to Headquarters for Naval Air Forces and Naval Air Force Pacific, the bulk of the Pacific Fleet's helicopter squadrons, and part of the West Coast <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a> fleet. <a href="/wiki/Naval_Amphibious_Base_Coronado" title="Naval Amphibious Base Coronado">NAB Coronado</a> is located on the southern end of the Coronado Island and is home to the navy's west coast SEAL teams and special boat units. NAB Coronado is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Special_Warfare_Center" title="Naval Special Warfare Center">Naval Special Warfare Center</a>, the primary training center for SEALs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The other major collection of naval bases on the west coast is in <a href="/wiki/Puget_Sound" title="Puget Sound">Puget Sound</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_(U.S._state)" title="Washington (U.S. state)">Washington</a>. Among them, <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Everett" title="Naval Station Everett">NS Everett</a> is one of the newer bases and the navy states that it is its most modern facility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAS_Fallon" title="NAS Fallon">NAS Fallon</a>, Nevada serves as the primary training ground for navy strike aircrews, and is home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Strike_Air_Warfare_Center" title="Naval Strike Air Warfare Center">Naval Strike Air Warfare Center</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Master_Jet_Base" title="Master Jet Base">Master Jet Bases</a> are also located at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAS_Lemoore" title="NAS Lemoore">NAS Lemoore</a>, California and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAS_Whidbey_Island" title="NAS Whidbey Island">NAS Whidbey Island</a>, Washington, while the carrier-based airborne early warning aircraft community and major air test activities are located at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAS_Point_Mugu" title="NAS Point Mugu">NAS Point Mugu</a>, California. The naval presence in Hawaii is centered on <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Pearl_Harbor" title="Naval Station Pearl Harbor">NS Pearl Harbor</a>, which hosts the headquarters of the Pacific Fleet and many of its subordinate commands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_territories">United States territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: United States territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_030527-N-0000X-001_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Carl_Vinson_(CVN_70)_pier_side_in_Apra_Harbor,_Guam.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/US_Navy_030527-N-0000X-001_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Carl_Vinson_%28CVN_70%29_pier_side_in_Apra_Harbor%2C_Guam.jpg/220px-US_Navy_030527-N-0000X-001_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Carl_Vinson_%28CVN_70%29_pier_side_in_Apra_Harbor%2C_Guam.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/US_Navy_030527-N-0000X-001_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Carl_Vinson_%28CVN_70%29_pier_side_in_Apra_Harbor%2C_Guam.jpg/330px-US_Navy_030527-N-0000X-001_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Carl_Vinson_%28CVN_70%29_pier_side_in_Apra_Harbor%2C_Guam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/US_Navy_030527-N-0000X-001_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Carl_Vinson_%28CVN_70%29_pier_side_in_Apra_Harbor%2C_Guam.jpg/440px-US_Navy_030527-N-0000X-001_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Carl_Vinson_%28CVN_70%29_pier_side_in_Apra_Harbor%2C_Guam.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_030527-N-0000X-001_The_aircraft_carrier_USS_Carl_Vinson_(CVN_70)_pier_side_in_Apra_Harbor,_Guam.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_Carl_Vinson_(CVN-70)" title="USS Carl Vinson (CVN-70)">USS <i>Carl Vinson</i> (CVN-70)</a> pier side in <a href="/wiki/Apra_Harbor" title="Apra Harbor">Apra Harbor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Guam#Villages_and_military_bases" title="Guam">Guam</a>, an island strategically located in the Western Pacific Ocean, maintains a sizable U.S. Navy presence, including <a href="/wiki/Naval_Base_Guam" title="Naval Base Guam">NB Guam</a>. The westernmost U.S. territory, it contains a natural deep water harbor capable of harboring aircraft carriers in emergencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Its naval air station was deactivated<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> in 1995 and its flight activities transferred to nearby <a href="/wiki/Andersen_Air_Force_Base" title="Andersen Air Force Base">Andersen Air Force Base</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> in the Caribbean formerly housed <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Roads_Naval_Station" title="Roosevelt Roads Naval Station">NS Roosevelt Roads</a>, which was shut down in 2004 shortly after the controversial closure of the live ordnance training area on nearby <a href="/wiki/Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Vieques, Puerto Rico">Vieques Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_2-8"><a href="#cite_note-status-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_countries">Foreign countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Foreign countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The largest overseas base is the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fleet_Activities_Yokosuka" title="United States Fleet Activities Yokosuka">United States Fleet Activities Yokosuka</a>, Japan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> which serves as the home port for the navy's largest forward-deployed fleet and is a significant base of operations in the Western Pacific.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>European operations revolve around facilities in Italy (<a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Sigonella" title="Naval Air Station Sigonella">NAS Sigonella</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naval_Computer_and_Telecommunications_Station_Naples,_Italy" title="Naval Computer and Telecommunications Station Naples, Italy">Naval Computer and Telecommunications Station Naples</a>) with <a href="/wiki/Naval_Support_Activity_Naples" title="Naval Support Activity Naples">NSA Naples</a> as the homeport for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Sixth_Fleet" title="United States Sixth Fleet">Sixth Fleet</a> and Command Naval Region Europe, Africa, Southwest Asia (CNREURAFSWA), and additional facilities in nearby <a href="/wiki/Gaeta" title="Gaeta">Gaeta</a>. There is also <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Rota,_Spain" title="Naval Station Rota, Spain">NS Rota</a> in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and NSA <a href="/wiki/Souda_Bay" title="Souda Bay">Souda Bay</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the Middle East, naval facilities are located almost exclusively in countries bordering the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Naval_Support_Activity_Bahrain" title="Naval Support Activity Bahrain">NSA Bahrain</a> serving as the headquarters of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Naval_Forces_Central_Command" title="U.S. Naval Forces Central Command">U.S. Naval Forces Central Command</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Fifth_Fleet" title="U.S. Fifth Fleet">U.S. Fifth Fleet</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_Naval_Base" title="Guantanamo Bay Naval Base">NS Guantanamo Bay</a> in Cuba is the oldest overseas facility and has become known in recent years as the location of a <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_detention_camp" title="Guantanamo Bay detention camp">detention camp</a> for suspected <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> operatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ForeignFacilities_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-ForeignFacilities-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Equipment">Equipment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Equipment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equipment_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Equipment of the United States Navy">Equipment of the United States Navy</a></div>
<p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the navy operates over 280 ships, 3,650+ aircraft, 50,000 non-combat vehicles and owns 75,200 buildings on 3,300,000 acres (13,000 km<sup>2</sup>). In addition, the Navy has more than one hundred vessels operated by the Military Sealift Command (MSC) crewed by a combination of civilian contractors and a small number of uniformed Naval personnel.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ships">Ships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Ships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Navy_ships" title="List of United States Navy ships">List of United States Navy ships</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_current_ships_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="List of current ships of the United States Navy">List of current ships of the United States Navy</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_currently_active_United_States_military_watercraft" title="List of currently active United States military watercraft">List of currently active United States military watercraft</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_ships" title="United States Navy ships">United States Navy ships</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_States_ship_naming_conventions" title="United States ship naming conventions">United States ship naming conventions</a></div>
<p>The names of commissioned ships of the U.S. Navy are prefixed with the letters "USS", designating "United States Ship".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Non-commissioned, civilian-manned vessels of the navy have names that begin with "USNS", standing for "United States Naval Ship" The names of ships are officially selected by the secretary of the navy, often to honor important people or places.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Additionally, each ship is given a letter-based <a href="/wiki/Hull_classification_symbol" title="Hull classification symbol">hull classification symbol</a> (for example, CVN or DDG) to indicate the vessel's type and number. All ships in the navy inventory are placed in the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Vessel_Register" title="Naval Vessel Register">Naval Vessel Register</a>, which is part of "the Navy List" (required by article 29 of the United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (July 2013)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata">– <a href="/wiki/Talk:United_States_Navy#Dubious" title="Talk:United States Navy">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> The register tracks data such as the current status of a ship, the date of its commissioning, and the date of its decommissioning. Vessels that are removed from the register prior to disposal are said to be <i>stricken</i> from the register. The navy also maintains a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_reserve_fleets" title="United States Navy reserve fleets">reserve fleet</a> of inactive vessels that are maintained for reactivation in times of need.</p>
<p>The U.S. Navy was one of the first to install <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactors</a> aboard naval vessels;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> today, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear energy</a> powers all active U.S. aircraft carriers and <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a>. In the case of the <a href="/wiki/Nimitz-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Nimitz-class aircraft carrier"><i>Nimitz</i>-class</a> carrier, two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_reactor" title="United States Naval reactor">naval reactors</a> give the ship almost unlimited range and provide enough electrical energy to power a city of 100,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The U.S. Navy previously operated <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_powered_cruisers_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Nuclear powered cruisers of the United States Navy">nuclear-powered cruisers</a>, but all have been decommissioned.</p>
<p>The U.S. Navy had identified a need for 313 combat ships in early 2010s, but under its plans at the time could only afford 232 to 243.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In March 2014, the Navy started counting self-deployable support ships such as minesweepers, surveillance craft, and tugs in the "battle fleet" in order to reach a count of 272 as of October 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> and it includes ships that have been put in "shrink wrap".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft_carriers">Aircraft carriers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Aircraft carriers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Nimitz_in_Victoria_Canada_036.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3032" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/USS_Nimitz_in_Victoria_Canada_036.jpg/220px-USS_Nimitz_in_Victoria_Canada_036.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/USS_Nimitz_in_Victoria_Canada_036.jpg/330px-USS_Nimitz_in_Victoria_Canada_036.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/USS_Nimitz_in_Victoria_Canada_036.jpg/440px-USS_Nimitz_in_Victoria_Canada_036.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Nimitz_in_Victoria_Canada_036.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_Nimitz_(CVN-68)" title="USS Nimitz (CVN-68)">USS <i>Nimitz</i> (CVN-68)</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Nimitz-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Nimitz-class aircraft carrier"><i>Nimitz</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_aircraft_carriers_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="List of aircraft carriers of the United States Navy">List of aircraft carriers of the United States Navy</a></div>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a> is typically deployed along with a host of additional vessels, forming a <a href="/wiki/Carrier_strike_group" title="Carrier strike group">carrier strike group</a>. The supporting ships, which usually include three or four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aegis_combat_system" title="Aegis combat system">Aegis</a>-equipped cruisers and destroyers, a frigate, and two attack submarines, are tasked with protecting the carrier from air, missile, sea, and undersea threats as well as providing additional strike capabilities themselves. Ready logistics support for the group is provided by a combined ammunition, oiler, and supply ship. Modern carriers are named after American admirals and politicians, usually presidents.</p>
<p>The Navy has a statutory requirement for a minimum of 11 aircraft carriers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Currently there are 10 that are deployable and one, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_Gerald_R._Ford_(CVN-78)" title="USS Gerald R. Ford (CVN-78)">USS <i>Gerald R. Ford</i> (CVN-78)</a>, is currently undergoing extensive systems and technologies testing until around 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USNIdeploy_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-USNIdeploy-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Amphibious_warfare_vessels">Amphibious warfare vessels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Amphibious warfare vessels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Bataan_(LHD-5);10080504.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1680" data-file-width="2100" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/USS_Bataan_%28LHD-5%29%3B10080504.jpg/220px-USS_Bataan_%28LHD-5%29%3B10080504.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/USS_Bataan_%28LHD-5%29%3B10080504.jpg/330px-USS_Bataan_%28LHD-5%29%3B10080504.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/USS_Bataan_%28LHD-5%29%3B10080504.jpg/440px-USS_Bataan_%28LHD-5%29%3B10080504.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Bataan_(LHD-5);10080504.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Bataan_(LHD-5)" title="USS Bataan (LHD-5)">USS <i>Bataan</i> (LHD-5)</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Wasp-class_amphibious_assault_ship" title="Wasp-class amphibious assault ship"><i>Wasp</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_assault_ship" title="Amphibious assault ship">amphibious assault ship</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LPD-17_Class.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="918" data-file-width="1324" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/LPD-17_Class.jpg/220px-LPD-17_Class.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/LPD-17_Class.jpg/330px-LPD-17_Class.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/LPD-17_Class.jpg/440px-LPD-17_Class.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LPD-17_Class.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_San_Antonio_(LPD-17)" title="USS San Antonio (LPD-17)">USS <i>San Antonio</i> (LPD-17)</a>, a <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio-class_amphibious_transport_dock" title="San Antonio-class amphibious transport dock"><i>San Antonio</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_transport_dock" title="Amphibious transport dock">amphibious transport dock</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Navy_amphibious_warfare_ships" title="List of United States Navy amphibious warfare ships">List of United States Navy amphibious warfare ships</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amphibious_assault_ship" title="Amphibious assault ship">Amphibious assault ships</a> are the centerpieces of US amphibious warfare and fulfill the same power projection role as aircraft carriers except that their striking force centers on land forces instead of aircraft. They deliver, command, coordinate, and fully support all elements of a 2,200-strong <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_Expeditionary_Unit" title="Marine Expeditionary Unit">Marine Expeditionary Unit</a> in an amphibious assault using both air and amphibious vehicles. Resembling small aircraft carriers, amphibious assault ships are capable of <a href="/wiki/V/STOL" title="V/STOL">V/STOL</a>, <a href="/wiki/STOVL" title="STOVL">STOVL</a>, <a href="/wiki/VTOL" title="VTOL">VTOL</a>, tiltrotor, and rotary wing aircraft operations. They also contain a <a href="/wiki/Well_deck" title="Well deck">well deck</a> to support the use of <a href="/wiki/Landing_Craft_Air_Cushion" title="Landing Craft Air Cushion">Landing Craft Air Cushion</a> (LCAC) and other amphibious assault watercraft. Recently, amphibious assault ships have begun to be deployed as the core of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expeditionary_strike_group" title="Expeditionary strike group">expeditionary strike group</a>, which usually consists of an additional <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_transport_dock" title="Amphibious transport dock">amphibious transport dock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dock_landing_ship" title="Dock landing ship">dock landing ship</a> for amphibious warfare and an Aegis-equipped cruiser and destroyer, frigate, and attack submarine for group defense. Amphibious assault ships are typically named after World War II aircraft carriers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amphibious_transport_docks" title="Amphibious transport docks">Amphibious transport docks</a> are warships that embark, transport, and land Marines, supplies, and equipment in a supporting role during amphibious warfare missions. With a landing platform, amphibious transport docks also have the capability to serve as secondary aviation support for an expeditionary group. All amphibious transport docks can operate helicopters, LCACs, and other conventional amphibious vehicles while the newer <i>San Antonio</i> class of ships has been explicitly designed to operate all three elements of the Marines' "mobility triad": <a href="/wiki/Expeditionary_Fighting_Vehicle" title="Expeditionary Fighting Vehicle">Expeditionary Fighting Vehicles</a> (EFVs), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V-22_Osprey" title="V-22 Osprey">V-22 Osprey</a> tiltrotor aircraft, and LCACs. Amphibious transport docks are named after U.S. cities, with the exception of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_John_P._Murtha_(LPD-26)" title="USS John P. Murtha (LPD-26)">USS <i>John P. Murtha</i> (LPD-26)</a>, named after a former Congressman and USMC Officer and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_Mesa_Verde_(LPD-19)" title="USS Mesa Verde (LPD-19)">USS <i>Mesa Verde</i> (LPD-19)</a>, named for <a href="/wiki/Mesa_Verde_National_Park" title="Mesa Verde National Park">Mesa Verde National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dock_landing_ship" title="Dock landing ship">dock landing ship</a> is a medium amphibious transport that is designed specifically to support and operate LCACs, though it is able to operate other amphibious assault vehicles in the United States inventory as well. Dock landing ships are normally deployed as a component of an expeditionary strike group's amphibious assault contingent, operating as a secondary launch platform for LCACs. All dock landing ships are named after cities or important places in U.S. and U.S. Naval history.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cruisers">Cruisers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cruisers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cruisers_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="List of cruisers of the United States Navy">List of cruisers of the United States Navy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_030903-N-5024R-003_USS_Port_Royal_(DDG_73)_departed_on_deployment.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/US_Navy_030903-N-5024R-003_USS_Port_Royal_%28DDG_73%29_departed_on_deployment.jpg/220px-US_Navy_030903-N-5024R-003_USS_Port_Royal_%28DDG_73%29_departed_on_deployment.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/US_Navy_030903-N-5024R-003_USS_Port_Royal_%28DDG_73%29_departed_on_deployment.jpg/330px-US_Navy_030903-N-5024R-003_USS_Port_Royal_%28DDG_73%29_departed_on_deployment.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/US_Navy_030903-N-5024R-003_USS_Port_Royal_%28DDG_73%29_departed_on_deployment.jpg/440px-US_Navy_030903-N-5024R-003_USS_Port_Royal_%28DDG_73%29_departed_on_deployment.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_030903-N-5024R-003_USS_Port_Royal_(DDG_73)_departed_on_deployment.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Port_Royal_(CG-73)" title="USS Port Royal (CG-73)">USS <i>Port Royal</i> (CG-73)</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Ticonderoga-class_cruiser" title="Ticonderoga-class cruiser"><i>Ticonderoga</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Cruiser" title="Cruiser">cruiser</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cruiser" title="Cruiser">Cruisers</a> are large surface combat vessels that conduct anti-air/anti-missile warfare, surface warfare, anti-submarine warfare, and strike operations independently or as members of a larger task force. Modern guided missile cruisers were developed out of a need to counter the <a href="/wiki/Anti-ship_missile" title="Anti-ship missile">anti-ship missile</a> threat facing the United States Navy. This led to the development of the <a href="/wiki/AN/SPY-1" title="AN/SPY-1">AN/SPY-1</a> phased array radar and the <a href="/wiki/RIM-67_Standard" title="RIM-67 Standard">Standard missile</a> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aegis_combat_system" title="Aegis combat system">Aegis combat system</a> coordinating the two. <a href="/wiki/Ticonderoga-class_cruiser" title="Ticonderoga-class cruiser"><i>Ticonderoga</i>-class</a> cruisers were the first to be equipped with Aegis and were put to use primarily as anti-air and anti-missile defense in a battle force protection role. Later developments of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertical_launch_system" title="Vertical launch system">vertical launch systems</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BGM-109_Tomahawk" title="BGM-109 Tomahawk">Tomahawk missile</a> gave cruisers additional long-range land and sea strike capability, making them capable of both offensive and defensive battle operations. The <i>Ticonderoga</i> class is the only active class of cruiser. All cruisers in this class are named after battles.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Destroyers">Destroyers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Destroyers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_destroyers_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="List of destroyers of the United States Navy">List of destroyers of the United States Navy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Future_USS_Zumwalt%27s_first_underway_at_sea.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3455" data-file-width="5523" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Future_USS_Zumwalt%27s_first_underway_at_sea.jpg/220px-Future_USS_Zumwalt%27s_first_underway_at_sea.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Future_USS_Zumwalt%27s_first_underway_at_sea.jpg/330px-Future_USS_Zumwalt%27s_first_underway_at_sea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Future_USS_Zumwalt%27s_first_underway_at_sea.jpg/440px-Future_USS_Zumwalt%27s_first_underway_at_sea.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Future_USS_Zumwalt%27s_first_underway_at_sea.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_Zumwalt_(DDG-1000)" title="USS Zumwalt (DDG-1000)">USS <i>Zumwalt</i> (DDG-1000)</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Zumwalt-class_destroyer" title="Zumwalt-class destroyer"><i>Zumwalt</i> -class</a> <a href="/wiki/Stealth_ship" title="Stealth ship">stealth</a> <a href="/wiki/Guided_missile_destroyer" title="Guided missile destroyer">guided missile destroyer</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Destroyers" title="Destroyers">Destroyers</a> are multi-mission medium surface ships capable of sustained performance in anti-air, anti-submarine, anti-ship, and offensive strike operations. Like cruisers, guided missile destroyers are primarily focused on surface strikes using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BGM-109_Tomahawk" title="BGM-109 Tomahawk">Tomahawk missiles</a> and fleet defense through Aegis and the Standard missile. Destroyers additionally specialize in anti-submarine warfare and are equipped with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ASROC" title="ASROC">VLA rockets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikorsky_SH-60_Seahawk" title="Sikorsky SH-60 Seahawk">LAMPS Mk III Sea Hawk</a> helicopters to deal with underwater threats. When deployed with a carrier strike group or expeditionary strike group, destroyers and their fellow Aegis-equipped cruisers are primarily tasked with defending the fleet while providing secondary strike capabilities. With very few exceptions, destroyers are named after U.S. Navy, Marine Corps, and Coast Guard heroes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Frigates_and_Littoral_combat_ships">Frigates and Littoral combat ships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Frigates and Littoral combat ships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_frigates_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="List of frigates of the United States Navy">List of frigates of the United States Navy</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Littoral_combat_ship" title="Littoral combat ship">Littoral combat ship</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Independence_LCS-2_at_pierce_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="874" data-file-width="1309" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/USS_Independence_LCS-2_at_pierce_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-USS_Independence_LCS-2_at_pierce_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/USS_Independence_LCS-2_at_pierce_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-USS_Independence_LCS-2_at_pierce_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/USS_Independence_LCS-2_at_pierce_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-USS_Independence_LCS-2_at_pierce_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Independence_LCS-2_at_pierce_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Independence_(LCS-2)" title="USS Independence (LCS-2)">USS <i>Independence</i> (LCS-2)</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Littoral_combat_ship" title="Littoral combat ship">Littoral combat ship</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS-Freedom-130222-N-DR144-174-crop.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1426" data-file-width="1900" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/USS-Freedom-130222-N-DR144-174-crop.jpg/220px-USS-Freedom-130222-N-DR144-174-crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/USS-Freedom-130222-N-DR144-174-crop.jpg/330px-USS-Freedom-130222-N-DR144-174-crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/USS-Freedom-130222-N-DR144-174-crop.jpg/440px-USS-Freedom-130222-N-DR144-174-crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS-Freedom-130222-N-DR144-174-crop.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Freedom_(LCS-1)" title="USS Freedom (LCS-1)">USS <i>Freedom</i> (LCS-1)</a> underway in special <a href="/wiki/Dazzle_camouflage" title="Dazzle camouflage">naval camouflage</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Modern U.S. <a href="/wiki/Frigate" title="Frigate">frigates</a> mainly perform anti-submarine warfare for carrier and expeditionary strike groups and provide armed escort for supply convoys and merchant shipping. They are designed to protect friendly ships against hostile submarines in low to medium threat environments, using torpedoes and LAMPS helicopters. Independently, frigates are able to conduct counterdrug missions and other maritime interception operations. As in the case of destroyers, frigates are named after U.S. Navy, Marine Corps, and Coast Guard heroes. As of autumn 2015, the U.S. Navy has retired its most recent class of frigates, and expects that by 2020 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Littoral_Combat_Ship" title="Littoral Combat Ship">Littoral Combat Ships</a> (LCS) will assume many of the duties the frigate had with the fleet. The LCS is a class of relatively small surface vessels intended for operations in the littoral zone (close to shore). It was "envisioned to be a networked, agile, stealthy surface combatant capable of defeating anti-access and asymmetric threats in the littorals". They have the capabilities of a small assault transport, including a flight deck and hangar for housing two helicopters, a stern ramp for operating small boats, and the cargo volume and payload to deliver a small assault force with fighting vehicles to a roll-on/roll-off port facility. The ship is easy to reconfigure for different roles, including <a href="/wiki/Anti-submarine_warfare" title="Anti-submarine warfare">anti-submarine warfare</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mine_countermeasures" title="Mine countermeasures">mine countermeasures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anti-surface_warfare" title="Anti-surface warfare">anti-surface warfare</a>, intelligence, surveillance and reconnaissance, homeland defense, maritime intercept, special operations, and logistics, all by swapping mission-specific modules as needed. The LCS program is still relatively new as of 2015 with only a few active ships, but the navy has announced plans for up to 32 ships. (See: <a href="/wiki/Littoral_combat_ship#List_of_LCS_ships" title="Littoral combat ship">List of littoral combat ships</a>) The navy has announced that a further 20 vessels to be built after that will be redesignated as 'frigates'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>In addition, <a href="/wiki/USS_Constitution" title="USS Constitution">USS <i>Constitution</i></a>, commissioned in 1797 and one of the <a href="/wiki/Original_six_frigates_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Original six frigates of the United States Navy">original six frigates of the United States Navy</a>, remains in commission at the Charlestown Navy Yard in Boston. She serves as a tribute to the heritage of the Navy, and occasionally sails for commemorative events such as <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(United_States)" title="Independence Day (United States)">Independence Day</a> and various victories during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>. <i>Constitution</i> is currently the oldest commissioned warship afloat. <a href="/wiki/HMS_Victory" title="HMS Victory">HMS <i>Victory</i></a> is older, and in commission, but is in permanent drydock.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mine_countermeasures_ships">Mine countermeasures ships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Mine countermeasures ships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mine_warfare_vessels_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="List of mine warfare vessels of the United States Navy">List of mine warfare vessels of the United States Navy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uss_warrior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1880" data-file-width="2860" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Uss_warrior.jpg/220px-Uss_warrior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Uss_warrior.jpg/330px-Uss_warrior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Uss_warrior.jpg/440px-Uss_warrior.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uss_warrior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Warrior_(MCM-10)" title="USS Warrior (MCM-10)">USS <i>Warrior</i> (MCM-10)</a> in port</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mine_countermeasures_vessel" title="Mine countermeasures vessel">Mine countermeasures vessels</a> are a combination of <a href="/wiki/Minehunter" title="Minehunter">minehunters</a>, a naval vessel that actively detects and destroys individual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_mines" title="Naval mines">naval mines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Minesweeper" title="Minesweeper">minesweepers</a>, which clear mined areas as a whole, without prior detection of the mines. The navy has approximately a dozen of these in active service, but the mine countermeasure (MCM) role is also being assumed by the incoming classes of littoral combat ships. MCM vessels have mostly legacy names of previous US Navy ships, especially WWII-era minesweepers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Patrol_boats">Patrol boats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Patrol boats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_patrol_vessels_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="List of patrol vessels of the United States Navy">List of patrol vessels of the United States Navy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Typhoon_(PC-5).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1632" data-file-width="2464" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/USS_Typhoon_%28PC-5%29.jpg/220px-USS_Typhoon_%28PC-5%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/USS_Typhoon_%28PC-5%29.jpg/330px-USS_Typhoon_%28PC-5%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/USS_Typhoon_%28PC-5%29.jpg/440px-USS_Typhoon_%28PC-5%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Typhoon_(PC-5).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_Typhoon_(PC-5)" title="USS Typhoon (PC-5)">USS <i>Typhoon</i> (PC-5)</a> departing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Amphibious_Base_Little_Creek" title="Naval Amphibious Base Little Creek">Naval Amphibious Base Little Creek</a> in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Patrol_boat" title="Patrol boat">patrol boat</a> is a relatively small naval vessel generally designed for coastal defense duties. There have been many designs for patrol boats, though the navy currently only has a single class. They may be operated by a nation's navy or coast guard, and may be intended for marine ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_water" title="Blue water">blue water</a>") and/or estuarine or river ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brown_water" title="Brown water">brown water</a>") environments. The Navy has approximately a dozen in active service, which are mainly used in the littoral regions of the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>, but have also been used for home port patrols and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drug_interdiction" title="Drug interdiction">drug interdiction</a> missions. The navy's current class of patrol boats have names based on weather phenomena.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Submarines">Submarines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Submarines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Submarines_in_the_United_States_Navy" title="Submarines in the United States Navy">Submarines in the United States Navy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Kentucky_(SSBN-737).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="444" data-file-width="597" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/USS_Kentucky_%28SSBN-737%29.jpg/220px-USS_Kentucky_%28SSBN-737%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/USS_Kentucky_%28SSBN-737%29.jpg/330px-USS_Kentucky_%28SSBN-737%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/USS_Kentucky_%28SSBN-737%29.jpg/440px-USS_Kentucky_%28SSBN-737%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Kentucky_(SSBN-737).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Kentucky_(SSBN-737)" title="USS Kentucky (SSBN-737)">USS <i>Kentucky</i> (SSBN-737)</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Ohio-class_submarine" title="Ohio-class submarine"><i>Ohio</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile_submarine" title="Ballistic missile submarine">ballistic missile submarine</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_040730-N-1234E-002_PCU_Virginia_(SSN_774)_returns_to_the_General_Dynamics_Electric_Boat_shipyard.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3000" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_Navy_040730-N-1234E-002_PCU_Virginia_%28SSN_774%29_returns_to_the_General_Dynamics_Electric_Boat_shipyard.jpg/220px-US_Navy_040730-N-1234E-002_PCU_Virginia_%28SSN_774%29_returns_to_the_General_Dynamics_Electric_Boat_shipyard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_Navy_040730-N-1234E-002_PCU_Virginia_%28SSN_774%29_returns_to_the_General_Dynamics_Electric_Boat_shipyard.jpg/330px-US_Navy_040730-N-1234E-002_PCU_Virginia_%28SSN_774%29_returns_to_the_General_Dynamics_Electric_Boat_shipyard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_Navy_040730-N-1234E-002_PCU_Virginia_%28SSN_774%29_returns_to_the_General_Dynamics_Electric_Boat_shipyard.jpg/440px-US_Navy_040730-N-1234E-002_PCU_Virginia_%28SSN_774%29_returns_to_the_General_Dynamics_Electric_Boat_shipyard.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_040730-N-1234E-002_PCU_Virginia_(SSN_774)_returns_to_the_General_Dynamics_Electric_Boat_shipyard.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Virginia_(SSN-774)" title="USS Virginia (SSN-774)">USS <i>Virginia</i> (SSN-774)</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Virginia-class_submarine" title="Virginia-class submarine"><i>Virginia</i> -class</a> <a href="/wiki/Attack_submarine" title="Attack submarine">attack submarine</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>All current and planned U.S. Navy submarines are nuclear-powered, as only nuclear propulsion allows for the combination of stealth and long duration, high-speed sustained underwater movement that makes modern nuclear submarines so vital to a modern blue-water navy. The U.S. Navy operates three types: <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile_submarine" title="Ballistic missile submarine">ballistic missile submarines</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guided_missile_submarine" title="Guided missile submarine">guided missile submarines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Attack_submarine" title="Attack submarine">attack submarines</a>. U.S. Navy (nuclear) ballistic missile submarines carry the stealthiest leg of the U.S. strategic triad (the other legs are the land-based U.S. strategic missile force and the air-based U.S. strategic bomber force). These submarines have only one mission: to carry and, if called upon, to launch the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trident_nuclear_missile" title="Trident nuclear missile">Trident nuclear missile</a>. The primary missions of attack and guided missile submarines in the U.S. Navy are peacetime engagement, surveillance and intelligence, special operations, precision strikes, and control of the seas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> To these, attack submarines also add the battlegroup operations mission. Attack and guided missile submarines have several tactical missions, including sinking ships and other subs, launching <a href="/wiki/Cruise_missile" title="Cruise missile">cruise missiles</a>, gathering intelligence, and assisting in special operations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>As with other classes of naval vessels, most U.S. submarines (or "boats") are named according to specific conventions. The boats of the current U.S. ballistic missile submarine class, <a href="/wiki/Ohio-class_submarine" title="Ohio-class submarine"><i>Ohio</i>-class</a>, are named after U.S. states. As the four current U.S. guided missile submarines are converted <i>Ohio</i>-class boats, they have retained their U.S. state names. The members of the oldest currently-commissioned attack submarine class, the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles-class_submarine" title="Los Angeles-class submarine"><i>Los Angeles</i> class</a>, are typically named for cities. The follow-on <a href="/wiki/Seawolf-class_submarine" title="Seawolf-class submarine"><i>Seawolf</i>-class</a>' three submarines—<i>Seawolf</i>, <i>Connecticut</i> and <i>Jimmy Carter</i>—share no consistent naming scheme. With the current <a href="/wiki/Virginia-class_submarine" title="Virginia-class submarine"><i>Virginia</i>-class</a> class attack submarines, the U.S. Navy has extended the <i>Ohio</i> class' state-based naming scheme to these submarines. Attack submarines prior to the <i>Los Angeles</i> class were named for denizens of the deep, while pre-<i>Ohio</i>-class ballistic missile submarines were named for famous Americans and foreigners with notable connections to the United States.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft">Aircraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Aircraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Four_Super_Hornets.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3008" data-file-width="1960" height="338" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Four_Super_Hornets.jpg/220px-Four_Super_Hornets.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Four_Super_Hornets.jpg/330px-Four_Super_Hornets.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Four_Super_Hornets.jpg/440px-Four_Super_Hornets.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Four_Super_Hornets.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Four Navy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F/A-18E/F_Super_Hornet" title="F/A-18E/F Super Hornet">F/A-18F Super Hornets</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_naval_aircraft" title="List of United States naval aircraft">List of United States naval aircraft</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_military_aircraft_of_the_United_States_(naval)" title="List of military aircraft of the United States (naval)">List of military aircraft of the United States (naval)</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Navy_aircraft_squadrons" title="List of United States Navy aircraft squadrons">List of United States Navy aircraft squadrons</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_active_United_States_military_aircraft" title="List of active United States military aircraft">List of active United States military aircraft</a></div>
<p>Carrier-based aircraft are able to strike air, sea, and land targets far from a carrier strike group while protecting friendly forces from enemy aircraft, ships, and submarines. In peacetime, aircraft's ability to project the threat of sustained attack from a mobile platform on the seas gives United States leaders significant diplomatic and crisis-management options. Aircraft additionally provide logistics support to maintain the navy's readiness and, through helicopters, supply platforms with which to conduct <a href="/wiki/Search_and_rescue" title="Search and rescue">search and rescue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Special_operations" title="Special operations">special operations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anti-submarine_warfare" title="Anti-submarine warfare">anti-submarine warfare</a> (ASW), and <a href="/wiki/Anti-surface_warfare" title="Anti-surface warfare">anti-surface warfare</a> (ASuW).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The U.S. Navy began to research the use of aircraft at sea in the 1910s, with Lieutenant Theodore G. "Spuds" Ellyson becoming the first naval aviator on 28 January 1911, and commissioned its first aircraft carrier, <a href="/wiki/USS_Langley_(CV-1)" title="USS Langley (CV-1)">USS <i>Langley</i> (CV-1)</a>, in 1922.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> United States naval aviation fully came of age in World War II, when it became clear following the <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">Attack on Pearl Harbor</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea" title="Battle of the Coral Sea">Battle of the Coral Sea</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">Battle of Midway</a> that aircraft carriers and the planes that they carried had replaced the battleship as the greatest weapon on the seas. Leading navy aircraft in World War II included the <a href="/wiki/Grumman_F4F_Wildcat" title="Grumman F4F Wildcat">Grumman F4F Wildcat</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grumman_F6F_Hellcat" title="Grumman F6F Hellcat">Grumman F6F Hellcat</a>, the Chance <a href="/wiki/Vought_F4U_Corsair" title="Vought F4U Corsair">Vought F4U Corsair</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Douglas_SBD_Dauntless" title="Douglas SBD Dauntless">Douglas SBD Dauntless</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Grumman_TBF_Avenger" title="Grumman TBF Avenger">Grumman TBF Avenger</a>. Navy aircraft also played a significant role in conflicts during the following Cold War years, with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-4_Phantom_II" title="F-4 Phantom II">F-4 Phantom II</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-14_Tomcat" title="F-14 Tomcat">F-14 Tomcat</a> becoming military icons of the era. The navy's current primary fighter and attack airplanes are the multi-mission <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F/A-18_Hornet" title="F/A-18 Hornet">F/A-18C/D Hornet</a> and its newer cousin, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F/A-18E/F_Super_Hornet" title="F/A-18E/F Super Hornet">F/A-18E/F Super Hornet</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-35_Lightning_II" title="F-35 Lightning II">F-35 Lightning II</a> is presently under development and was scheduled to replace the C and D versions of the Hornet beginning in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Initial operational capability of the F-35C is now expected to be February 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The Navy is also looking to eventually replace its F/A-18E/F Super Hornets with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F/A-XX" title="F/A-XX">F/A-XX</a> program.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The Aircraft Investment Plan sees naval aviation growing from 30 percent of current aviation forces to half of all procurement funding over the next three decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Weapons">Weapons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Weapons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Navy_weapons" title="List of United States Navy weapons">List of United States Navy weapons</a></div>
<p>Current U.S. Navy shipboard weapons systems are almost entirely focused on missiles, both as a weapon and as a threat. In an offensive role, missiles are intended to strike targets at long distances with accuracy and precision. Because they are unmanned weapons, missiles allow for attacks on heavily defended targets without risk to human pilots. Land strikes are the domain of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BGM-109_Tomahawk" title="BGM-109 Tomahawk">BGM-109 Tomahawk</a>, which was first deployed in the 1980s and is continually being updated to increase its capabilities. For anti-ship strikes, the navy's dedicated missile is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harpoon_Missile" title="Harpoon Missile">Harpoon Missile</a>. To defend against enemy missile attack, the navy operates a number of systems that are all coordinated by the Aegis combat system. Medium-long range defense is provided by the <a href="/wiki/RIM-67_Standard" title="RIM-67 Standard">Standard Missile 2</a>, which has been deployed since the 1980s. The Standard missile doubles as the primary shipboard anti-aircraft weapon and is undergoing development for use in theater ballistic missile defense. Short range defense against missiles is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Phalanx_CIWS" title="Phalanx CIWS">Phalanx CIWS</a> and the more recently developed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESSM" title="ESSM">RIM-162 Evolved Sea Sparrow Missile</a>. In addition to missiles, the navy employs <a href="/wiki/Mark_46_torpedo" title="Mark 46 torpedo">Mark 46</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_50_torpedo" title="Mark 50 torpedo">Mark 50 torpedoes</a> and various types of naval mines.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_050112-N-5345W-074_Aviation_Ordnancemen_prepare_to_load_500-pound_laser_guided_bombs_(GBU-12)_onto_weapon_pylons_under_an_F-14B_Tomcat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/US_Navy_050112-N-5345W-074_Aviation_Ordnancemen_prepare_to_load_500-pound_laser_guided_bombs_%28GBU-12%29_onto_weapon_pylons_under_an_F-14B_Tomcat.jpg/220px-US_Navy_050112-N-5345W-074_Aviation_Ordnancemen_prepare_to_load_500-pound_laser_guided_bombs_%28GBU-12%29_onto_weapon_pylons_under_an_F-14B_Tomcat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/US_Navy_050112-N-5345W-074_Aviation_Ordnancemen_prepare_to_load_500-pound_laser_guided_bombs_%28GBU-12%29_onto_weapon_pylons_under_an_F-14B_Tomcat.jpg/330px-US_Navy_050112-N-5345W-074_Aviation_Ordnancemen_prepare_to_load_500-pound_laser_guided_bombs_%28GBU-12%29_onto_weapon_pylons_under_an_F-14B_Tomcat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/US_Navy_050112-N-5345W-074_Aviation_Ordnancemen_prepare_to_load_500-pound_laser_guided_bombs_%28GBU-12%29_onto_weapon_pylons_under_an_F-14B_Tomcat.jpg/440px-US_Navy_050112-N-5345W-074_Aviation_Ordnancemen_prepare_to_load_500-pound_laser_guided_bombs_%28GBU-12%29_onto_weapon_pylons_under_an_F-14B_Tomcat.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_050112-N-5345W-074_Aviation_Ordnancemen_prepare_to_load_500-pound_laser_guided_bombs_(GBU-12)_onto_weapon_pylons_under_an_F-14B_Tomcat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aviation Ordnancemen loading <a href="/wiki/GBU-12_Paveway_II" title="GBU-12 Paveway II">GBU-12</a> bombs in 2005.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Naval fixed-wing aircraft employ much of the same weapons as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a> for both air-to-air and air-to-surface combat. Air engagements are handled by the heat-seeking <a href="/wiki/AIM-9_Sidewinder" title="AIM-9 Sidewinder">Sidewinder</a> and the radar guided <a href="/wiki/AIM-120_AMRAAM" title="AIM-120 AMRAAM">AMRAAM</a> missiles along with the <a href="/wiki/M61_Vulcan" title="M61 Vulcan">M61 Vulcan</a> cannon for close range dogfighting.
