For surface strikes, navy aircraft utilize a combination of missiles, smart bombs, and dumb bombs. On the list of available missiles are the <a href="/wiki/AGM-65_Maverick" title="AGM-65 Maverick">Maverick</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standoff_Land_Attack_Missile" title="Standoff Land Attack Missile">SLAM-ER</a> and <a href="/wiki/AGM-154_Joint_Standoff_Weapon" title="AGM-154 Joint Standoff Weapon">JSOW</a>. Smart bombs include the GPS-guided <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JDAM" title="JDAM">JDAM</a> and the laser-guided <a href="/wiki/Paveway" title="Paveway">Paveway</a> series. Unguided munitions such as dumb bombs and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cluster_bomb" title="Cluster bomb">cluster bombs</a> make up the rest of the weapons deployed by fixed-wing aircraft.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Rotary aircraft weapons are focused on anti-submarine warfare (ASW) and light to medium surface engagements. To combat submarines, helicopters use Mark 46 and Mark 50 torpedoes. Against small watercraft, they utilize <a href="/wiki/AGM-114_Hellfire" title="AGM-114 Hellfire">Hellfire</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penguin_missile" title="Penguin missile">Penguin</a> air to surface missiles. Helicopters also employ various types of mounted anti-personnel machine guns, including the <a href="/wiki/M60_machine_gun" title="M60 machine gun">M60</a>, <a href="/wiki/M240_machine_gun" title="M240 machine gun">M240</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GAU-16" title="GAU-16">GAU-16/A</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Minigun" title="Minigun">GAU-17/A</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Nuclear weapons in the U.S. Navy arsenal are deployed through ballistic missile submarines and aircraft. The <i>Ohio</i>-class submarine carries the latest iteration of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trident_missile" title="Trident missile">Trident missile</a>, a three-stage, <a href="/wiki/Submarine-launched_ballistic_missile" title="Submarine-launched ballistic missile">submarine-launched ballistic missile</a> (SLBM) with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MIRV" title="MIRV">MIRV</a> capability; the current Trident II (D5) version is expected to be in service past 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The navy's other nuclear weapon is the air-deployed <a href="/wiki/B61_nuclear_bomb" title="B61 nuclear bomb">B61 nuclear bomb</a>. The B61 is a thermonuclear device that can be dropped by strike aircraft such as the F/A-18 Hornet and Super Hornet at high speed from a large range of altitudes. It can be released through free-fall or parachute and can be set to detonate in the air or on the ground.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Naval_jack">Naval jack</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Naval jack">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Naval_Jack_of_the_United_States.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="1330" height="53" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Naval_Jack_of_the_United_States.svg/100px-Naval_Jack_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Naval_Jack_of_the_United_States.svg/150px-Naval_Jack_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Naval_Jack_of_the_United_States.svg/200px-Naval_Jack_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="100"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Naval_Jack_of_the_United_States.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
U.S. Naval Jack</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Naval_Jack.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1482" height="71" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/US_Naval_Jack.svg/100px-US_Naval_Jack.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/US_Naval_Jack.svg/150px-US_Naval_Jack.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/US_Naval_Jack.svg/200px-US_Naval_Jack.svg.png 2x" width="100"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Naval_Jack.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FIAV_historical.svg"><img alt="FIAV historical.svg" data-file-height="150" data-file-width="230" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/FIAV_historical.svg/23px-FIAV_historical.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/FIAV_historical.svg/35px-FIAV_historical.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/FIAV_historical.svg/46px-FIAV_historical.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a> <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FIAV_000001.svg"><img alt="FIAV 000001.svg" data-file-height="210" data-file-width="320" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/FIAV_000001.svg/23px-FIAV_000001.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/FIAV_000001.svg/35px-FIAV_000001.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/FIAV_000001.svg/46px-FIAV_000001.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a> Former U.S. Naval Jack</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maritime_flags#Jacks" title="Maritime flags">naval jack</a> of the United States is the <a href="/wiki/First_Navy_Jack" title="First Navy Jack">First Navy Jack</a>, traditionally regarded as having been used during the American Revolutionary War. On 31 May 2002, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="Secretary of the Navy">Secretary of the Navy</a> <a href="/wiki/Gordon_R._England" title="Gordon R. England">Gordon R. England</a> directed all U.S. naval ships to fly the First Navy Jack for the duration of the "<a href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" title="War on Terror">War on Terror</a>". Many ships chose to shift colors later that year on the first anniversary of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/September_11,_2001_attacks" title="September 11, 2001 attacks">September 11, 2001 attacks</a>. The previous naval jack was a blue field with 50 white stars, identical to the canton of the <a href="/wiki/Ensign" title="Ensign">ensign</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_States" title="Flag of the United States">flag of the United States</a>) both in appearance and size, and remains in use with vessels of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Coast_Guard" title="U.S. Coast Guard">U.S. Coast Guard</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a>. A jack of similar design was used in 1794, though with 13 stars arranged in a 3–2–3–2–3 pattern. When a ship is moored or anchored, the jack is flown from the <a href="/wiki/Bow_(ship)" title="Bow (ship)">bow</a> of the ship while the ensign is flown from the <a href="/wiki/Stern" title="Stern">stern</a>. When underway, the ensign is raised on the mainmast. The First Naval Jack, however, has always been flown on the oldest ship in the active American fleet, which is currently <a href="/wiki/USS_Blue_Ridge_(LCC-19)" title="USS Blue Ridge (LCC-19)">USS <i>Blue Ridge</i> (LCC-19)</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_sailors">Notable sailors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Notable sailors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Navy_people" title="List of United States Navy people">List of United States Navy people</a></div>
<p>Many past and present United States historical figures have served in the navy. Notable officers include <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones" title="John Paul Jones">John Paul Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Barry_(naval_officer)" title="John Barry (naval officer)">John Barry</a> (<a href="/wiki/Continental_Navy" title="Continental Navy">Continental Navy</a> officer and first flag officer of the United States Navy),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edward_Preble" title="Edward Preble">Edward Preble</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Lawrence" title="James Lawrence">James Lawrence</a> (whose <a href="/wiki/Last_words" title="Last words">last words</a> "don't give up the ship" are memorialized in <a href="/wiki/Bancroft_Hall" title="Bancroft Hall">Bancroft Hall</a> at the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">United States Naval Academy</a>), <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Decatur" title="Stephen Decatur">Stephen Decatur, Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Farragut" title="David Farragut">David Farragut</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Dixon_Porter" title="David Dixon Porter">David Dixon Porter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Hazard_Perry" title="Oliver Hazard Perry">Oliver Hazard Perry</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matthew_Perry_(naval_officer)" title="Matthew Perry (naval officer)">Commodore Matthew Perry</a> (whose <a href="/wiki/Black_Ships" title="Black Ships">Black Ships</a> forced the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Kanagawa" title="Convention of Kanagawa">opening of Japan</a>), <a href="/wiki/George_Dewey" title="George Dewey">George Dewey</a> (the only person in the history of the United States to have attained the rank of Admiral of the Navy), and the officers who attained the rank of Fleet Admiral during World War II: <a href="/wiki/William_D._Leahy" title="William D. Leahy">William D. Leahy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ernest_J._King" title="Ernest J. King">Ernest J. King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chester_W._Nimitz" title="Chester W. Nimitz">Chester W. Nimitz</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_F._Halsey,_Jr." title="William F. Halsey, Jr.">William F. Halsey, Jr.</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The first American <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">president</a> who served in the navy was <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> (who commanded the famous <i><a href="/wiki/Motor_Torpedo_Boat_PT-109" title="Motor Torpedo Boat PT-109">PT-109</a></i>). Others included <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>. Both <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> were the <a href="/wiki/Assistant_Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="Assistant Secretary of the Navy">assistant secretary of the navy</a> prior to their presidencies. Many members of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a> served in the navy, notably <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Senator" title="United States Senator">U.S. Senators</a> <a href="/wiki/Bob_Kerrey" title="Bob Kerrey">Bob Kerrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>. Other notable former members of the U.S. Navy include astronauts, entertainers, authors and professional athletes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
